‭Abstract‬
‭The‬‭interaction‬‭between‬‭the‬‭T-cell‬‭receptor‬‭(TCR)‬‭and‬‭an‬‭antigen‬‭peptide‬‭displayed‬‭by‬‭the‬
‭major‬ ‭histocompatibility‬ ‭complex‬ ‭(MHC)‬ ‭molecule‬ ‭plays‬ ‭a‬ ‭vital‬ ‭role‬ ‭in‬ ‭initiating‬ ‭the‬ ‭T‬
‭cell-mediated‬ ‭response‬ ‭within‬ ‭the‬ ‭adaptive‬ ‭immune‬ ‭system.‬ ‭Being‬ ‭able‬ ‭to‬ ‭predict‬ ‭which‬
‭peptides‬‭TCR‬‭is‬‭able‬‭to‬‭bind‬‭to,‬‭that‬‭is‬‭its‬‭specificity,‬‭is‬‭of‬‭great‬‭interest‬‭in‬‭areas‬‭of‬‭vaccine‬
‭development,‬‭cancer‬‭treatment‬‭and‬‭treatment‬‭of‬‭autoimmune‬‭diseases.‬‭A‬‭wealth‬‭of‬‭models‬
‭for‬‭solving‬‭this‬‭task‬‭have‬‭been‬‭developed‬‭over‬‭the‬‭past‬‭years.‬‭They‬‭all‬‭however‬‭struggle‬‭to‬
‭predict‬‭specificity‬‭for‬‭peptides‬‭that‬‭have‬‭low‬‭similarity‬‭to‬‭the‬‭ones‬‭they‬‭were‬‭trained‬‭on,‬‭and‬
‭which‬ ‭they‬ ‭have‬ ‭never‬ ‭encountered‬ ‭before‬‭or‬‭only‬‭seen‬‭a‬‭few‬‭examples‬‭of.‬‭Here,‬‭it‬‭was‬
‭investigated‬ ‭if‬ ‭neural‬ ‭networks‬ ‭for‬ ‭prediction‬ ‭of‬ ‭TCR‬ ‭specificity‬ ‭would‬ ‭benefit‬ ‭from‬ ‭using‬
‭language‬ ‭models‬ ‭to‬ ‭embed‬ ‭their‬ ‭input‬ ‭sequences‬ ‭instead‬ ‭of‬ ‭using‬ ‭a‬ ‭more‬ ‭standard‬
‭BLOSUM-based‬ ‭encoding.‬ ‭Input‬ ‭sequences‬ ‭were‬ ‭embedded‬ ‭by‬ ‭three‬ ‭different‬ ‭language‬
‭models‬‭of‬‭the‬‭type‬‭called‬‭transformers,‬‭namely‬‭ESM-1b,‬‭ProtT5-XL-U50‬‭and‬‭ESM-2.‬‭These‬
‭language‬‭models‬‭had‬‭all‬‭been‬‭pre-trained‬‭on‬‭huge‬‭datasets‬‭to‬‭learn‬‭the‬‭general‬‭aspects‬‭of‬
‭protein‬‭sequences.‬‭The‬‭networks‬‭applied‬‭were‬‭variants‬‭of‬‭the‬‭NetTCR‬‭convolutional‬‭neural‬
‭network (CNN) max-pooled architecture.‬
‭For‬‭all‬‭three‬‭transformers,‬‭the‬‭produced‬‭embedded‬‭input‬‭sequences‬‭were‬‭found‬‭to‬‭result‬‭in‬
‭enhanced‬‭prediction‬‭of‬‭TCR‬‭specificity‬‭over‬‭the‬‭BLOSUM‬‭encoded‬‭input‬‭sequences.‬‭Of‬‭the‬
‭three‬‭transformers‬‭ESM-1b‬‭led‬‭to‬‭the‬‭best‬‭model‬‭performance,‬‭only‬‭being‬‭slightly‬‭better‬‭than‬
‭the other two.‬
‭In‬‭all‬‭cases,‬‭proper‬‭scaling‬‭of‬‭the‬‭input‬‭space,‬‭choice‬‭of‬‭network‬‭activation‬‭function‬‭and‬‭the‬
‭dimensions of the neural network were found to influence the predictive power.‬
‭In‬‭conclusion‬‭it‬‭was‬‭possible‬‭to‬‭significantly‬‭enhance‬‭TCR‬‭specificity‬‭prediction‬‭when‬‭utilizing‬
‭embedded‬ ‭sequences‬ ‭as‬ ‭input,‬ ‭as‬ ‭opposed‬ ‭to‬ ‭sequences‬ ‭encoded‬ ‭with‬ ‭BLOSUM.‬ ‭To‬
‭achieve optimal performance, fine-tuning of hyperparameters would be necessary.‬
‭1‬

==PAGE:8==
‭1 Introduction‬
‭T‬‭cells‬‭play‬‭a‬‭vital‬‭role‬‭in‬‭the‬‭adaptive‬‭immune‬‭system,‬‭orchestrating‬‭and‬‭carrying‬‭out‬‭attacks‬
‭on‬‭pathogens‬‭that‬‭manage‬‭to‬‭evade‬‭the‬‭initial‬‭defenses‬‭of‬‭the‬‭innate‬‭immune‬‭system.‬‭They‬
‭detect‬ ‭the‬ ‭presence‬ ‭of‬ ‭intracellular‬ ‭pathogens‬ ‭by‬ ‭binding‬ ‭to‬ ‭antigens‬ ‭displayed‬ ‭on‬ ‭the‬
‭surface‬‭of‬‭infected‬‭cells.‬‭These‬‭antigens‬‭consist‬‭of‬‭small‬‭peptide‬‭fragments,‬‭derived‬‭from‬‭the‬
‭pathogen’s‬ ‭proteins,‬ ‭bound‬ ‭to‬ ‭proteins‬ ‭called‬ ‭major‬ ‭histocompatibility‬ ‭complex‬ ‭(MHC)‬
‭molecules‬‭(Jensen‬‭2023;‬‭Murphy‬‭and‬‭Weaver‬‭2016)‬‭.‬‭The‬‭recognition‬‭of‬‭antigens‬‭by‬‭T‬‭cells‬
‭is‬ ‭facilitated‬ ‭by‬‭the‬‭T-cell‬‭receptor‬‭(TCR).‬‭The‬‭interaction‬‭between‬‭TCR‬‭and‬‭peptide:MHC‬
‭(pMHC)‬‭molecules‬‭thus‬‭forms‬‭an‬‭essential‬‭step‬‭in‬‭the‬‭immune‬‭response‬‭of‬‭T‬‭cells.‬‭Not‬‭every‬
‭MHC-presented‬‭peptide‬‭can‬‭engage‬‭in‬‭an‬‭interaction‬‭with‬‭TCR,‬‭and‬‭conversely,‬‭individual‬
‭TCRs‬ ‭establish‬ ‭highly‬ ‭specific‬ ‭interactions‬ ‭only‬‭with‬‭a‬‭limited‬‭range‬‭of‬‭pMHC‬‭complexes.‬
‭Being‬‭able‬‭to‬‭predict‬‭the‬‭specificity‬‭of‬‭TCR‬‭to‬‭peptides‬‭is‬‭of‬‭great‬‭interest‬‭in‬‭areas‬‭of‬‭vaccine‬
‭development,‬ ‭cancer‬ ‭treatment‬ ‭and‬ ‭treatment‬ ‭of‬ ‭autoimmune‬ ‭diseases‬ ‭(Montemurro,‬
‭Jessen, and Nielsen 2022; Jensen and Nielsen 2023)‬‭.‬
‭T‬‭cells‬‭fall‬‭into‬‭two‬‭major‬‭classes‬‭distinguished‬‭by‬‭their‬‭ability‬‭to‬‭recognize‬‭different‬‭classes‬
‭of‬‭MHC‬‭molecules.‬‭This‬‭project‬‭will‬‭only‬‭deal‬‭with‬‭prediction‬‭of‬‭TCR‬‭specificity‬‭in‬‭the‬‭class‬‭of‬
‭T‬ ‭cells‬ ‭called‬ ‭cytotoxic‬ ‭T‬ ‭cells.‬ ‭They‬ ‭recognize‬ ‭MHC‬ ‭class‬ ‭I‬ ‭(MHC-I)‬ ‭molecules‬‭and‬‭are‬
‭responsible‬‭for‬‭killing‬‭other‬‭cells‬‭that‬‭have‬‭been‬‭infected‬‭with‬‭intracellular‬‭pathogens,‬‭such‬
‭as viruses‬‭(Jensen 2023)‬‭.‬
‭1.1 The TCR Structure‬
‭The‬‭TCR‬‭is‬‭a‬‭heterodimer‬‭most‬‭often‬‭composed‬‭of‬‭an‬‭α‬‭and‬‭a‬‭β‬‭polypeptide‬‭chain,‬‭termed‬
‭TCRα‬‭and‬‭TCRβ,‬‭respectively.‬‭A‬‭minority‬‭of‬‭TCRs‬‭are‬‭made‬‭up‬‭of‬‭a‬‭γ‬‭and‬‭a‬‭δ‬‭chain‬‭instead.‬
‭Since‬‭the‬‭α‬‭and‬‭a‬‭β‬‭chains‬‭are‬‭by‬‭far‬‭the‬‭most‬‭commonly‬‭observed,‬‭this‬‭project‬‭will‬‭only‬‭deal‬
‭with TCRs consisting of this pair of polypeptide chains.‬
‭TCRα‬ ‭and‬ ‭TCRβ‬ ‭each‬ ‭consist‬ ‭of‬ ‭a‬ ‭variable‬ ‭region‬ ‭and‬ ‭a‬ ‭constant‬ ‭region.‬ ‭The‬
‭antigen-binding‬‭site‬‭of‬‭TCR‬‭is‬‭located‬‭on‬‭the‬‭variable‬‭region‬‭of‬‭the‬‭chains‬‭and‬‭defined‬‭by‬‭six‬
‭loops,‬‭three‬‭on‬‭each‬‭α‬‭and‬‭β‬‭chain.‬‭They‬‭determine‬‭the‬‭specificity‬‭of‬‭TCR‬‭and‬‭are‬‭denoted‬
‭complementarity-determining‬‭regions‬‭1-3‬‭(CDRs‬‭1-3).‬‭The‬‭CDR3s‬‭primarily‬‭interact‬‭with‬‭the‬
‭peptide,‬‭while‬‭the‬‭CDR1s‬‭and‬‭CDR2s‬‭mainly‬‭interact‬‭with‬‭MHC.‬‭The‬‭TCR‬‭specificity‬‭for‬‭a‬
‭given‬‭peptide‬‭is‬‭thus‬‭mainly‬‭defined‬‭by‬‭the‬‭CDR3s,‬‭but‬‭the‬‭CDR1s‬‭and‬‭CDR2s‬‭also‬‭play‬‭an‬
‭important‬ ‭role‬ ‭due‬ ‭to‬ ‭their‬ ‭interaction‬ ‭with‬ ‭MHC‬ ‭(Jensen‬ ‭2023;‬ ‭Montemurro‬ ‭et‬ ‭al.‬ ‭2021;‬
‭Murphy‬‭and‬‭Weaver‬‭2016)‬‭.‬‭An‬‭illustration‬‭of‬‭the‬‭interaction‬‭between‬‭TCR‬‭and‬‭a‬‭pMHC‬‭class‬
‭I (pMHC-I) complex is shown in fig. 1.1.‬
‭4‬
==PAGE:9==
‭Fig.‬‭1.1.‬‭Schematic‬‭of‬‭interactions‬‭between‬‭TCR‬‭and‬‭the‬‭pMHC-I‬‭complex.‬‭It‬‭is‬‭illustrated‬‭how‬‭the‬‭CDRs‬‭of‬
‭TCR‬‭interact‬‭with‬‭the‬‭pMHC-I‬‭complex.‬‭The‬‭TCR‬‭is‬‭depicted‬‭at‬‭the‬‭top,‬‭with‬‭the‬‭α‬‭chain‬‭shown‬‭in‬‭pink‬‭and‬‭the‬‭β‬
‭chain‬‭shown‬‭in‬‭green.‬‭The‬‭CDRs‬‭are‬‭also‬‭all‬‭color‬‭coded.‬‭The‬‭pMHC-I‬‭complex‬‭is‬‭depicted‬‭at‬‭the‬‭bottom‬‭with‬‭the‬
‭MHC-I‬‭molecule‬‭shown‬‭in‬‭maroon‬‭and‬‭the‬‭peptide‬‭shown‬‭in‬‭black.‬‭The‬‭figure‬‭is‬‭an‬‭adaptation‬‭of‬‭fig.‬‭2d‬‭from‬‭(La‬
‭Gruta et al. 2018)‬‭.‬
‭1.2 V(D)J recombination‬
‭Peptides‬‭bound‬‭to‬‭the‬‭pMHC-I‬‭complex‬‭typically‬‭have‬‭lengths‬‭ranging‬‭from‬‭9‬‭to‬‭11‬‭amino‬
‭acids‬‭(Trolle‬‭et‬‭al.‬‭2016)‬‭,‬‭which‬‭allows‬‭for‬‭a‬‭considerable‬‭variety‬‭of‬‭amino‬‭acid‬‭sequences‬‭to‬
‭be‬ ‭presented‬ ‭to‬ ‭TCR.‬ ‭However,‬ ‭the‬ ‭diversity‬ ‭is‬ ‭significantly‬ ‭constrained‬ ‭by‬ ‭the‬ ‭specific‬
‭peptide‬ ‭sequences‬ ‭that‬ ‭can‬ ‭bind‬ ‭to‬ ‭the‬ ‭MHC.‬ ‭An‬ ‭event‬ ‭known‬ ‭as‬ ‭V(D)J‬ ‭recombination,‬
‭happening‬‭during‬‭T-cell‬‭maturation,‬‭is‬‭responsible‬‭for‬‭producing‬‭the‬‭necessary‬‭diversity‬‭of‬
‭the‬‭CDRs‬‭to‬‭be‬‭able‬‭to‬‭recognize‬‭the‬‭multitude‬‭of‬‭peptides‬‭(Jensen‬‭2023)‬‭.‬‭This‬‭results‬‭in‬‭an‬
‭immense repertoire of different TCRs.‬
‭The‬‭germline‬‭DNA‬‭of‬‭a‬‭developing‬‭T‬‭cell‬‭contains‬‭multiple‬‭copies‬‭of‬‭gene‬‭segments,‬‭called‬
‭variable‬‭(V),‬‭diversity‬‭(D)‬‭and‬‭joining‬‭(J)‬‭gene‬‭segments.‬‭They‬‭are‬‭randomly‬‭rearranged‬‭in‬
‭V(D)J‬ ‭recombination‬ ‭to‬ ‭form‬ ‭the‬ ‭exons‬ ‭for‬ ‭the‬ ‭variable‬ ‭region‬ ‭of‬ ‭TCRα‬ ‭and‬ ‭TCRβ.‬ ‭The‬
‭rearrangement‬‭involves‬‭randomly‬‭selecting‬‭only‬‭one‬‭type‬‭of‬‭each‬‭gene‬‭segment‬‭and‬‭joining‬
‭them‬ ‭together‬ ‭to‬ ‭create‬ ‭an‬ ‭exon.‬ ‭The‬ ‭TCRβ‬ ‭locus‬ ‭encompasses‬ ‭all‬ ‭three‬‭types‬‭of‬‭gene‬
‭segments,‬‭meaning‬‭that‬‭the‬‭V(D)J‬‭recombination‬‭for‬‭the‬‭β‬‭chain‬‭involves‬‭all‬‭three‬‭types‬‭of‬
‭gene‬‭segments‬‭(see‬‭fig‬‭1.2b).‬‭The‬‭TCRα‬‭locus‬‭on‬‭the‬‭other‬‭hand‬‭only‬‭contains‬‭the‬‭V‬‭and‬‭J‬
‭gene‬ ‭segments,‬ ‭which‬ ‭means‬ ‭that‬ ‭the‬ ‭V(D)J‬ ‭recombination‬ ‭for‬‭the‬‭α‬‭chain‬‭only‬‭involves‬
‭these‬ ‭two‬ ‭types‬ ‭of‬ ‭gene‬ ‭segments‬ ‭(see‬ ‭fig.‬ ‭1.2a).‬ ‭The‬ ‭higher‬ ‭number‬ ‭of‬ ‭types‬ ‭of‬ ‭gene‬
‭segments‬ ‭ending‬ ‭up‬ ‭in‬ ‭the‬ ‭exon‬ ‭for‬ ‭the‬ ‭variable‬ ‭region‬ ‭of‬ ‭the‬ ‭β‬ ‭chain,‬ ‭means‬ ‭a‬ ‭higher‬
‭diversity of the β chain compared to the α chain.‬
‭Besides‬‭rearranging‬‭gene‬‭segments,‬‭V(D)J‬‭recombination‬‭also‬‭involves‬‭random‬‭addition‬‭and‬
‭deletion‬ ‭of‬ ‭nucleotides‬ ‭in‬ ‭the‬ ‭junctions‬ ‭between‬ ‭joined‬ ‭gene‬ ‭segments,‬ ‭which‬ ‭further‬
‭increases the diversity of TCRs (see fig. 1.2).‬
‭The‬‭human‬‭genome‬‭encodes‬‭47‬‭V‬‭genes‬‭and‬‭61‬‭J‬‭genes‬‭for‬‭the‬‭α-chain,‬‭while‬‭54‬‭V‬‭genes,‬
‭2‬‭D‬‭genes‬‭and‬‭14‬‭J‬‭genes‬‭are‬‭encoded‬‭for‬‭the‬‭β-chain‬‭(La‬‭Gruta‬‭et‬‭al.‬‭2018)‬‭.‬‭All‬‭in‬‭all‬‭V(D)J‬
‭5‬
==PAGE:10==
‭recombination‬ ‭theoretically‬ ‭permits‬ ‭the‬ ‭formation‬ ‭of‬ ‭approximately‬
‭-‬
‭unique‬
‭combinations of TCR sequences in humans‬‭(La Gruta et al. 2018)‬‭.‬
‭After‬‭V(D)J‬‭recombination,‬‭the‬‭variable‬‭region‬‭exon‬‭for‬‭each‬‭of‬‭the‬‭two‬‭chains,‬‭is‬‭joined‬‭to‬‭a‬
‭constant‬‭region‬‭(C-region)‬‭sequence‬‭that‬‭encodes‬‭for‬‭the‬‭constant‬‭region‬‭of‬‭the‬‭respective‬
‭chain. This is done by RNA splicing after transcription (see fig. 1.2).‬
‭In‬‭the‬‭variable‬‭region‬‭exons‬‭of‬‭the‬‭two‬‭chains,‬‭the‬‭V‬‭and‬‭J‬‭gene‬‭segments,‬‭and‬‭in‬‭the‬‭case‬
‭of‬ ‭the‬ ‭β‬ ‭chain‬ ‭also‬ ‭the‬ ‭D‬ ‭segment,‬ ‭all‬ ‭share‬‭a‬‭region‬‭that‬‭codes‬‭for‬‭CDR3.‬‭This‬‭shared‬
‭region‬ ‭contributes‬ ‭to‬ ‭CDR3‬ ‭having‬ ‭the‬ ‭highest‬ ‭sequence‬ ‭variability‬‭among‬‭all‬‭the‬‭CDRs.‬
‭Furthermore,‬ ‭it‬ ‭is‬ ‭in‬ ‭this‬ ‭region‬ ‭that‬ ‭addition‬ ‭and‬ ‭deletion‬ ‭of‬ ‭nucleotides‬ ‭between‬ ‭gene‬
‭segment‬ ‭junctions‬ ‭has‬ ‭taken‬ ‭place,‬ ‭which‬ ‭further‬ ‭increases‬ ‭the‬ ‭diversity‬ ‭of‬ ‭the‬ ‭CDR3‬
‭sequence.‬‭In‬‭contrast‬‭the‬‭CDR1‬‭and‬‭CDR2‬‭are‬‭exclusively‬‭encoded‬‭by‬‭the‬‭V‬‭gene‬‭segment‬
‭(see fig. 1.2)‬‭(Jensen 2023; Murphy and Weaver 2016)‬‭.‬
‭Fig.‬‭1.2.‬‭Genomic‬‭organization‬‭and‬‭recombination‬‭of‬‭TCRα‬‭(a)‬‭and‬‭TCRβ‬‭(b)‬‭genes.‬‭Vertical‬‭lines‬‭with‬‭boxes‬
‭on‬‭top‬‭illustrate‬‭sequences.‬‭In‬‭both‬‭(a)‬‭and‬‭(b)‬‭the‬‭top‬‭sequence‬‭illustrates‬‭the‬‭germline‬‭DNA‬‭and‬‭its‬‭organization‬
‭of‬‭gene‬‭segments‬‭involved‬‭in‬‭V(D)J‬‭recombination‬‭as‬‭well‬‭as‬‭the‬‭genes‬‭coding‬‭for‬‭the‬‭C-region‬‭of‬‭the‬‭respective‬
‭chain.‬‭The‬‭middle‬‭sequence‬‭is‬‭the‬‭messenger‬‭RNA‬‭resulting‬‭from‬‭V(D)J‬‭recombination,‬‭transcription‬‭and‬‭splicing‬
‭to‬‭the‬‭C-region‬‭sequence.‬‭It‬‭is‬‭depicted‬‭how‬‭the‬‭gene‬‭segments‬‭and‬‭the‬‭C-region‬‭sequence‬‭are‬‭joined‬‭together.‬
‭Nucleotide‬‭insertions‬‭and‬‭deletions‬‭between‬‭gene‬‭segment‬‭junctions‬‭are‬‭represented‬‭by‬‭black‬‭boxes.‬‭The‬‭bottom‬
‭part‬‭also‬‭shows‬‭the‬‭messenger‬‭RNA,‬‭but‬‭this‬‭time‬‭the‬‭location‬‭of‬‭the‬‭regions‬‭coding‬‭for‬‭CDRs‬‭are‬‭marked‬‭with‬
‭boxes‬‭colored‬‭as‬‭per‬‭fig.‬‭1.1.‬‭Between‬‭the‬‭middle‬‭and‬‭bottom‬‭sequence‬‭it‬‭is‬‭annotated‬‭where‬‭the‬‭regions‬‭coding‬
‭for‬‭the‬‭different‬‭CDRs‬‭are‬‭located‬‭on‬‭the‬‭gene‬‭segments.‬‭The‬‭figure‬‭is‬‭an‬‭adaptation‬‭of‬‭fig.‬‭2c‬‭from‬‭(La‬‭Gruta‬‭et‬
‭al. 2018)‬‭.‬
‭1.3 Existing Models for Prediction of TCR Specificity‬
‭During‬ ‭the‬ ‭past‬ ‭years,‬ ‭a‬ ‭wealth‬ ‭of‬ ‭models‬ ‭using‬ ‭CDR‬ ‭sequences‬ ‭for‬ ‭prediction‬ ‭of‬ ‭TCR‬
‭specificity‬ ‭to‬ ‭peptides‬ ‭have‬ ‭been‬ ‭developed.‬ ‭They‬ ‭can‬ ‭broadly‬ ‭be‬ ‭divided‬ ‭into‬ ‭two‬
‭categories,‬‭namely‬‭unsupervised‬‭distance-based‬‭approaches‬‭and‬‭supervised‬‭feature-based‬
‭approaches.‬‭In‬‭the‬‭distance-based‬‭approaches‬‭the‬‭specificity‬‭of‬‭a‬‭TCR‬‭is‬‭predicted‬‭by‬‭its‬
‭sequence‬ ‭similarity‬ ‭to‬ ‭other‬ ‭TCRs‬ ‭with‬ ‭known‬ ‭target‬ ‭peptides.‬ ‭The‬ ‭feature-based‬
‭approaches‬ ‭use‬ ‭machine‬ ‭learning‬ ‭models‬ ‭to‬ ‭identify‬ ‭underlying‬ ‭patterns‬ ‭in‬ ‭a‬ ‭dataset‬ ‭of‬
‭known‬ ‭TCR-peptide‬ ‭pair‬ ‭sequences.‬ ‭These‬ ‭learned‬ ‭patterns‬ ‭can‬‭then‬‭be‬‭used‬‭to‬‭predict‬
‭specificity‬‭for‬‭new‬‭unseen‬‭TCRs‬‭(Meysman‬‭et‬‭al.‬‭2023)‬‭.‬‭A‬‭non-exhaustive‬‭list‬‭of‬‭models‬‭from‬
‭the two categories is given here:‬
‭6‬
==PAGE:11==
‭In‬‭the‬‭feature-based‬‭category,‬‭we‬‭have‬‭convolutional‬‭neural‬‭network‬‭(CNN)‬‭models,‬‭such‬‭as‬
‭ImRex‬ ‭(Moris‬ ‭et‬ ‭al.‬ ‭2021)‬‭,‬ ‭TCRAI‬ ‭(W.‬ ‭Zhang‬ ‭et‬ ‭al.‬ ‭2021)‬ ‭and‬ ‭NetTCR‬ ‭2.2‬‭(Jensen‬‭and‬
‭Nielsen‬‭2023)‬‭,‬‭autoencoder-based‬‭models‬‭such‬‭as‬‭DeepTCR‬‭(Sidhom‬‭et‬‭al.‬‭2021)‬‭,‬‭decision‬
‭tree‬‭models‬‭such‬‭as‬‭SETE‬‭(Tong‬‭et‬‭al.‬‭2020)‬‭,‬‭Gaussian‬‭process‬‭models‬‭such‬‭as‬‭TCRGP‬
‭(Jokinen‬
‭et‬
‭al.‬ ‭2021)‬‭,‬ ‭as‬ ‭well‬ ‭as‬ ‭transformer-based‬ ‭models‬ ‭such‬ ‭as‬ ‭TULIP‬
‭(Meynard-Piganeau et al. 2023)‬‭.‬
‭In‬‭the‬‭distance-based‬‭category‬‭we‬‭have‬‭the‬‭models‬‭TCRdist3‬‭(Mayer-Blackwell‬‭et‬‭al.‬‭2021)‬‭,‬
‭GLIPH2‬ ‭(Huang‬ ‭et‬ ‭al.‬ ‭2020)‬ ‭and‬ ‭TCRbase‬ ‭(Montemurro,‬ ‭Jessen,‬ ‭and‬ ‭Nielsen‬ ‭2022)‬ ‭to‬
‭mention a few‬‭(Jensen and Nielsen 2023)‬‭.‬
‭In‬ ‭a‬‭recent‬‭benchmark‬‭(Meysman‬‭et‬‭al.‬‭2023)‬‭,‬‭it‬‭was‬‭found‬‭that‬‭similarity-based‬‭methods‬
‭perform‬ ‭almost‬ ‭on‬ ‭par‬ ‭with‬ ‭feature-based‬ ‭methods‬‭in‬‭the‬‭case‬‭of‬‭high‬‭similarity‬‭between‬
‭training‬‭and‬‭test‬‭data,‬‭however‬‭it‬‭has‬‭been‬‭shown‬‭(Montemurro,‬‭Jessen,‬‭and‬‭Nielsen‬‭2022)‬
‭that‬ ‭when‬ ‭the‬ ‭similarity‬ ‭is‬ ‭decreased‬ ‭the‬ ‭feature-based‬ ‭methods‬ ‭tend‬ ‭to‬ ‭surpass‬ ‭the‬
‭similarity-based ones.‬
‭In‬‭the‬‭aforementioned‬‭benchmark,‬‭it‬‭was‬‭also‬‭found‬‭that‬‭models‬‭that‬‭use‬‭both‬‭TCR‬‭chains‬
‭for‬ ‭prediction‬ ‭have‬ ‭vastly‬ ‭better‬ ‭performance‬ ‭than‬ ‭models‬ ‭that‬ ‭use‬ ‭one‬ ‭chain‬ ‭only.‬
‭Additionally,‬ ‭models‬ ‭that‬ ‭make‬ ‭use‬ ‭of‬ ‭all‬ ‭three‬ ‭CDRs‬ ‭were‬ ‭found‬ ‭to‬ ‭perform‬ ‭better‬‭than‬
‭models that use CDR3 only.‬
‭The‬‭primary‬‭challenge‬‭faced‬‭by‬‭all‬‭current‬‭models‬‭lies‬‭in‬‭their‬‭ability‬‭to‬‭generalize‬‭effectively‬
‭to‬‭peptides‬‭that‬‭exhibit‬‭low‬‭similarity‬‭to‬‭the‬‭ones‬‭they‬‭were‬‭trained‬‭on,‬‭and‬‭which‬‭they‬‭have‬
‭never‬‭encountered‬‭or‬‭have‬‭only‬‭encountered‬‭a‬‭few‬‭examples‬‭of.‬‭The‬‭scarcity‬‭of‬‭available‬
‭data for training is the main contributing factor to this issue‬‭(Jensen and Nielsen 2023)‬‭.‬
‭1.4 Problem Statement‬
‭This‬‭project‬‭builds‬‭upon‬‭a‬‭NetTCR‬‭model‬‭that‬‭is‬‭a‬‭feature-based‬‭CNN‬‭and‬‭uses‬‭all‬‭CDRs‬‭of‬
‭both‬‭chains.‬‭The‬‭input‬‭sequences‬‭to‬‭the‬‭model‬‭are‬‭BLOSUM50‬‭(Henikoff‬‭and‬‭Henikoff‬‭1992)‬
‭encoded‬‭to‬‭capture‬‭features‬‭of‬‭the‬‭CDRs‬‭and‬‭the‬‭peptide.‬‭The‬‭aim‬‭is‬‭to‬‭investigate‬‭if‬‭the‬
‭prediction‬‭of‬‭TCR‬‭specificity‬‭can‬‭be‬‭improved‬‭by‬‭using‬‭embedded‬‭sequences‬‭for‬‭the‬‭CDRs‬
‭as‬‭input‬‭to‬‭the‬‭model‬‭instead.‬‭The‬‭embeddings‬‭will‬‭be‬‭generated‬‭from‬‭pre-trained‬‭so-called‬
‭language‬ ‭models‬ ‭called‬ ‭transformers‬ ‭that‬ ‭have‬ ‭learned‬ ‭the‬ ‭general‬ ‭aspects‬ ‭of‬ ‭protein‬
‭sequences‬‭from‬‭huge‬‭datasets.‬‭The‬‭hope‬‭is‬‭that‬‭these‬‭learned‬‭general‬‭aspects‬‭will‬‭improve‬
‭the TCR specificity predictions for NetTCR.‬
‭7‬
==PAGE:12==
‭2 Background‬
‭2.1 Neural Networks‬
‭A‬‭neural‬‭network‬‭is‬‭a‬‭machine‬‭learning‬‭model.‬‭It‬‭is‬‭a‬‭function‬
‭that‬‭maps‬‭inputs‬
‭to‬‭outputs‬
‭and‬‭takes‬‭the‬‭parameters‬
‭.‬‭If‬‭we‬‭assume‬‭that‬‭there‬‭exists‬‭a‬‭correct‬‭mapping‬
‭from‬
‭to‬
‭through‬‭a‬‭function‬
‭,‬‭then‬‭the‬‭goal‬‭of‬‭the‬‭network‬‭is‬‭to‬‭approximate‬
‭by‬
‭learning‬ ‭the‬ ‭parameters‬
‭of‬
‭such‬ ‭that‬
‭gets‬ ‭close‬ ‭to‬
‭(Goodfellow,‬
‭Bengio,‬‭and‬‭Courville‬‭2016)‬‭.‬‭To‬‭understand‬‭neural‬‭networks‬‭we‬‭will‬‭initially‬‭focus‬‭on‬‭one‬‭of‬
‭the simplest classes of neural networks, namely the feedforward neural network (FNN).‬
‭2.1.1 Feedforward Neural Networks‬
‭A‬ ‭FNN‬ ‭like‬ ‭any‬ ‭other‬ ‭neural‬ ‭network‬ ‭consists‬ ‭of‬ ‭neurons,‬ ‭also‬ ‭called‬ ‭units,‬ ‭which‬ ‭are‬
‭connected‬‭to‬‭each‬‭other‬‭in‬‭a‬‭network.‬‭An‬‭input‬
‭is‬‭given‬‭to‬‭the‬‭input‬‭neurons‬‭of‬‭the‬‭network‬
‭and‬‭then‬‭the‬‭information‬‭is‬‭passed‬‭through‬‭this‬‭network,‬‭being‬‭transformed‬‭along‬‭the‬‭way‬
‭and‬‭ending‬‭at‬‭the‬‭output‬‭neurons,‬‭which‬‭produce‬‭an‬‭output‬
‭.‬‭Each‬‭neuron‬‭represents‬‭a‬
‭vector-to-scalar‬‭function,‬‭which‬‭takes‬‭in‬‭inputs‬‭from‬‭multiple‬‭neurons‬‭and‬‭outputs‬‭a‬‭single‬
‭value,‬‭the‬‭exception‬‭being‬‭the‬‭input‬‭neurons‬‭which‬‭each‬‭simply‬‭passes‬‭an‬‭entry‬‭from‬‭the‬
‭input‬ ‭vector‬ ‭to‬ ‭the‬ ‭neurons‬ ‭they‬ ‭are‬ ‭connected‬ ‭to.‬ ‭The‬ ‭input‬ ‭neurons‬ ‭can‬ ‭therefore‬ ‭be‬
‭thought‬‭of‬‭as‬‭identity‬‭functions.‬‭Each‬‭input‬‭to‬‭a‬‭non-input-neuron‬‭has‬‭an‬‭associated‬‭weight,‬
‭expressing‬ ‭the‬ ‭importance‬ ‭of‬ ‭the‬ ‭input‬ ‭in‬ ‭the‬ ‭function‬ ‭the‬ ‭neuron‬ ‭represents.‬ ‭To‬ ‭each‬
‭non-input-neuron‬‭there‬‭is‬‭also‬‭a‬‭bias‬‭that‬‭determines‬‭the‬‭threshold‬‭for‬‭when‬‭the‬‭function‬‭the‬
‭neuron‬‭represents‬‭should‬‭output‬‭a‬‭positive‬‭signal.‬‭The‬‭entire‬‭neural‬‭network‬‭represents‬‭the‬
‭aforementioned‬ ‭function‬
‭,‬ ‭where‬ ‭the‬ ‭weights‬ ‭and‬ ‭biases‬ ‭together‬ ‭constitute‬ ‭the‬
‭parameters‬
‭of the function‬‭(Bishop 2006; Goodfellow,‬‭Bengio, and Courville 2016)‬‭.‬
‭In‬ ‭a‬ ‭FNN‬ ‭information‬ ‭flows‬ ‭directly‬ ‭from‬
‭through‬ ‭an‬ ‭input‬‭layer‬‭of‬‭input‬‭neurons,‬‭then‬
‭through‬‭one‬‭or‬‭multiple‬‭intermediate‬‭layers‬‭called‬‭hidden‬‭layers‬‭and‬‭finally‬‭into‬‭the‬‭output‬
‭layer.‬‭No‬‭neuron‬‭has‬‭feedback‬‭connections‬‭in‬‭which‬‭the‬‭output‬‭of‬‭a‬‭neuron‬‭is‬‭fed‬‭back‬‭into‬
‭itself‬ ‭or‬ ‭into‬ ‭one‬ ‭of‬ ‭the‬ ‭neurons‬ ‭in‬ ‭its‬‭input‬‭chains.‬‭That‬‭is,‬‭a‬‭FNN‬‭does‬‭not‬‭contain‬‭any‬
‭closed‬‭directed‬‭cycles‬‭of‬‭connections.‬‭This‬‭is‬‭the‬‭reason‬‭why‬‭this‬‭class‬‭of‬‭neural‬‭networks‬
‭are‬ ‭called‬‭feedforward‬‭in‬‭contrast‬‭to‬‭recurrent‬‭neural‬‭networks‬‭which‬‭do‬‭include‬‭feedback‬
‭connections‬ ‭(Goodfellow,‬ ‭Bengio,‬ ‭and‬‭Courville‬‭2016)‬‭.‬‭A‬‭standard‬‭FNN‬‭consists‬‭of‬‭dense‬
‭layers‬‭with‬‭neurons‬‭densely‬‭connected,‬‭meaning‬‭that‬‭each‬‭neuron‬‭of‬‭a‬‭layer‬‭is‬‭connected‬‭to‬
‭every‬‭neuron‬‭of‬‭the‬‭preceding‬‭layer.‬‭In‬‭contrast‬‭to‬‭this,‬‭we‬‭have‬‭sparse‬‭FNNs‬‭with‬‭not‬‭all‬
‭possible‬‭connections‬‭within‬‭a‬‭layer‬‭being‬‭present,‬‭an‬‭example‬‭of‬‭this‬‭are‬‭the‬‭convolutional‬
‭neural‬‭networks‬‭which‬‭we‬‭will‬‭look‬‭at‬‭later.‬‭When‬‭counting‬‭the‬‭number‬‭of‬‭layers‬‭in‬‭a‬‭neural‬
‭network,‬‭the‬‭input‬‭layer‬‭is‬‭normally‬‭not‬‭counted,‬‭since‬‭it‬‭does‬‭not‬‭involve‬‭any‬‭calculations‬
‭(Bishop 2006)‬‭. A diagram of a standard two-layer FNN‬‭is shown in fig. 2.1.‬
‭8‬
==PAGE:13==
‭Fig.‬‭2.1.‬‭Diagram‬‭of‬‭a‬‭standard‬‭two-layer‬‭FNN.‬‭Neurons‬‭are‬‭shown‬‭as‬‭circular‬‭nodes,‬‭while‬‭inputs‬‭and‬‭outputs‬
‭to‬ ‭the‬ ‭network‬ ‭are‬ ‭shown‬ ‭as‬ ‭square‬ ‭nodes.‬ ‭Solid‬ ‭links‬ ‭between‬ ‭nodes‬ ‭represent‬ ‭connections.‬ ‭Dotted‬ ‭links‬
‭indicate‬ ‭that‬ ‭the‬ ‭neural‬ ‭network‬ ‭continues‬ ‭vertically‬ ‭in‬ ‭between‬ ‭nodes.‬‭Each‬‭neuron‬‭is‬‭labeled‬‭by‬‭the‬‭function‬
‭they‬ ‭represent,‬ ‭the‬ ‭exception‬ ‭being‬ ‭the‬‭neurons‬‭of‬‭the‬‭input‬‭layer‬‭that‬‭each‬‭just‬‭represent‬‭an‬‭identity‬‭function.‬
‭Input‬ ‭and‬ ‭outputs‬ ‭to‬ ‭the‬ ‭network‬ ‭are‬ ‭labeled‬ ‭by‬ ‭the‬ ‭input‬ ‭or‬ ‭output‬ ‭variable‬ ‭they‬ ‭represent.‬ ‭Some‬ ‭of‬ ‭the‬
‭connections‬‭are‬‭labeled‬‭by‬‭their‬‭associated‬‭weight.‬‭The‬‭arrow‬‭indicates‬‭the‬‭direction‬‭of‬‭information‬‭flow‬‭through‬
‭the network.‬
‭We‬‭will‬‭now‬‭look‬‭at‬‭the‬‭computational‬‭steps‬‭from‬‭input‬‭to‬‭output‬‭in‬‭a‬‭standard‬‭two-layer‬‭FNN.‬
‭As‬ ‭already‬ ‭mentioned,‬ ‭each‬ ‭non-input-neuron‬ ‭in‬ ‭the‬ ‭FNN‬ ‭represents‬ ‭a‬ ‭vector-to-scalar‬
‭function.‬‭In‬‭the‬‭first‬‭layer‬‭of‬‭the‬‭network,‬‭being‬‭also‬‭the‬‭hidden‬‭layer‬‭(since‬‭we‬‭do‬‭not‬‭count‬
‭the‬ ‭input‬ ‭layer)‬ ‭we‬‭have‬
‭neurons‬‭and‬‭thus‬
‭functions‬
‭,‬‭with‬‭the‬‭superscript‬
‭indicating‬‭the‬‭first‬‭layer‬‭and‬
‭being‬‭the‬‭index‬‭of‬‭the‬‭neuron.‬‭Each‬‭function‬‭has‬
‭two‬‭steps.‬‭First,‬‭it‬‭calculates‬‭an‬‭affine‬‭transformation‬‭(linear‬‭transformation‬‭with‬‭a‬‭bias‬‭term)‬
‭of‬‭all‬‭the‬‭outputs‬‭from‬‭the‬‭input‬‭layer‬
‭,‬‭where‬
‭with‬

‭neurons‬‭in‬‭the‬‭input‬‭layer‬‭and‬‭also‬‭the‬‭dimension‬‭of‬‭the‬‭input‬‭vector.‬‭Second,‬‭it‬‭applies‬‭a‬‭so‬
‭called‬‭nonlinear‬‭activation‬‭function‬
‭to‬‭the‬‭affine‬‭transformation‬‭to‬‭get‬‭the‬‭activation‬

‭By‬ ‭adding‬ ‭more‬ ‭layers‬ ‭and‬ ‭more‬ ‭neurons‬ ‭within‬ ‭a‬‭layer,‬‭a‬‭neural‬‭network‬‭can‬‭represent‬
‭functions‬‭of‬‭increasing‬‭complexity.‬‭In‬‭fact‬‭multiple‬‭studies‬‭have‬‭shown‬‭that‬‭a‬‭neural‬‭network‬
‭is‬ ‭capable‬ ‭of‬ ‭learning‬ ‭any‬ ‭function‬ ‭provided‬ ‭it‬ ‭has‬ ‭enough‬ ‭hidden‬ ‭neurons.‬ ‭They‬ ‭are‬
‭therefore‬ ‭said‬ ‭to‬ ‭be‬ ‭universal‬ ‭approximators‬ ‭(Goodfellow,‬ ‭Bengio,‬ ‭and‬ ‭Courville‬ ‭2016;‬
‭Bishop 2006)‬‭.‬
‭2.1.2 Activation Functions‬
‭The‬‭activation‬‭function‬‭plays‬‭an‬‭important‬‭role‬‭for‬‭how‬‭complex‬‭a‬‭function‬‭a‬‭neural‬‭network‬
‭can‬‭approximate.‬‭To‬‭see‬‭this‬‭we‬‭will‬‭remove‬‭it‬‭from‬‭the‬‭hidden‬‭layer‬‭of‬‭a‬‭standard‬‭two-layer‬
‭FNN (equation 2.5):‬
‭(2.6)‬
‭Where‬
‭and‬
‭.‬ ‭We‬ ‭see‬ ‭that‬ ‭the‬ ‭function‬ ‭of‬ ‭our‬ ‭neural‬
‭network‬‭just‬‭becomes‬‭a‬‭nonlinear‬‭function‬‭of‬‭an‬‭affine‬‭transformation‬‭of‬‭the‬‭input‬
‭.‬‭This‬‭is‬
‭just‬‭a‬‭linear‬‭model‬‭with‬‭an‬‭applied‬‭activation‬‭function‬‭(the‬‭inverse‬‭of‬‭a‬‭“link‬‭function”,‬‭known‬
‭from‬‭statistical‬‭literature).‬‭It‬‭is‬‭also‬‭of‬‭the‬‭same‬‭form‬‭as‬‭the‬‭function‬‭for‬‭the‬‭first‬‭layer‬‭of‬‭the‬
‭two-layer‬‭FNN‬‭(equation‬‭2.2),‬‭meaning‬‭that‬‭our‬‭two-layer‬‭FNN‬‭has‬‭become‬‭equivalent‬‭to‬‭a‬
‭one-layer‬‭FNN.‬‭That‬‭is‬‭by‬‭removing‬‭the‬‭activation‬‭function‬‭from‬‭the‬‭hidden‬‭layer,‬‭we‬‭have‬
‭effectively‬‭removed‬‭the‬‭hidden‬‭layer‬‭and‬‭greatly‬‭reduced‬‭the‬‭number‬‭of‬‭functions‬‭the‬‭FNN‬
‭can approximate.‬
‭The‬‭activation‬‭function‬‭is‬‭also‬‭important‬‭for‬‭the‬‭output‬‭neurons.‬‭Here,‬‭the‬‭choice‬‭of‬‭activation‬
‭function depends on the assumed distribution of the target variable‬
‭(Bishop 2006)‬‭.‬
‭Some‬‭examples‬‭of‬‭the‬‭activation‬‭function‬‭that‬‭are‬‭commonly‬‭used‬‭are‬‭the‬‭logistic‬‭sigmoid‬
‭function and the rectified linear unit (ReLU) function.‬
‭The‬‭logistic‬‭sigmoid‬‭function‬‭(fig.‬‭2.2a),‬‭often‬‭just‬‭called‬‭the‬‭sigmoid‬‭function‬‭for‬‭short,‬‭maps‬
‭its argument‬
‭from the domain‬
‭to the range‬
‭:‬
‭10‬
==PAGE:15==
‭(2.7)‬
‭This‬‭activation‬‭function‬‭is‬‭however‬‭found‬‭to‬ ‭pose‬‭challenges‬‭for‬‭optimization‬‭and‬‭has‬‭thus‬‭in‬
‭many‬‭applications‬‭been‬‭replaced‬‭by‬‭the‬‭simpler‬‭and‬‭more‬‭easily‬‭trainable‬‭ReLU‬‭function.‬‭It‬
‭is‬‭however‬‭still‬‭widely‬‭used‬‭on‬‭output‬‭neurons‬‭due‬‭to‬‭the‬‭fact‬‭that‬‭values‬‭in‬‭the‬‭interval‬
‭can‬‭be‬‭interpreted‬‭as‬‭probabilities,‬‭which‬‭are‬‭useful‬‭in‬‭binary‬‭classification‬‭problems.‬‭It‬‭is‬‭a‬
‭nonlinear‬‭function‬‭but‬‭becomes‬‭close‬‭to‬‭being‬‭linear‬‭when‬‭its‬‭argument‬‭gets‬‭close‬‭to‬‭zero‬
‭(see fig. 2.2a).‬
‭Since‬‭the‬‭derivative‬‭of‬‭activation‬‭functions‬‭are‬‭important‬‭for‬‭training‬‭of‬‭neural‬‭networks,‬‭we‬
‭will‬‭look‬‭at‬‭the‬‭derivative‬‭of‬‭the‬‭sigmoid‬‭function‬‭as‬‭well.‬‭In‬‭fig.‬‭2.2a‬‭it‬‭is‬‭observed‬‭that‬‭its‬
‭derivative‬‭reaches‬‭a‬‭maximum‬‭of‬‭0.25‬‭when‬
‭is‬‭zero‬‭and‬‭as‬
‭diverges‬‭from‬‭zero‬‭in‬‭either‬
‭direction, the derivative approaches zero.‬
‭The‬‭ReLU‬‭activation‬‭function‬‭(fig.‬‭2.2b)‬‭has‬‭become‬‭the‬‭preferred‬‭choice‬‭due‬‭to‬‭the‬‭fact‬‭that‬
‭it‬‭usually‬‭works‬‭very‬‭well‬‭and‬‭is‬‭fast‬‭to‬‭compute.‬‭It‬‭is‬‭a‬‭nonlinear‬‭function,‬‭but‬‭remains‬‭very‬
‭close‬ ‭to‬ ‭linear‬ ‭by‬ ‭being‬ ‭piecewise‬ ‭linear‬ ‭with‬ ‭two‬ ‭linear‬ ‭pieces.‬ ‭Given‬ ‭an‬ ‭argument‬
‭it‬
‭returns the maximum of the input and zero:‬
‭(2.8)‬
‭It‬‭zeros‬‭out‬‭negative‬‭numbers‬‭and‬‭keeps‬‭positive‬‭ones.‬‭When‬‭negative‬‭values‬‭are‬‭given‬‭to‬
‭ReLU,‬‭the‬‭derivative‬‭becomes‬‭zero‬‭and‬‭when‬‭the‬‭input‬‭is‬‭positive‬‭the‬‭derivative‬‭becomes‬
‭one (see fig. 2.2b)‬‭(A. Zhang et al. 2021)‬‭.‬
‭Fig.‬‭2.2.‬‭Activation‬‭functions‬‭and‬‭their‬‭derivatives.‬‭(a)‬‭Sigmoid‬‭function.‬‭The‬‭sigmoid‬‭activation‬‭function‬‭and‬
‭its derivative.‬‭(b) ReLU function.‬‭The ReLU activation function and its derivative.‬
‭2.1.3 Loss Function‬
‭When‬‭training‬‭a‬‭neural‬‭network,‬‭we‬‭aim‬‭to‬‭learn‬‭the‬‭weights‬
‭and‬‭bias‬
‭parameters‬‭of‬‭the‬
‭function‬
‭that‬‭our‬‭neural‬‭network‬‭represents‬‭in‬‭order‬‭to‬‭approximate‬‭the‬‭true‬
‭function‬
‭.‬‭We‬‭can‬‭measure‬‭how‬‭well‬‭the‬‭approximation‬‭is‬‭doing‬‭as‬‭function‬‭of‬
‭and‬
‭by a so-called loss function.‬
‭11‬
==PAGE:16==
‭Let‬‭us‬‭look‬‭at‬‭the‬‭example‬‭of‬‭binary‬‭classification,‬‭where‬‭we‬‭wish‬‭to‬‭classify‬‭an‬‭observation‬
‭to‬‭one‬‭of‬‭two‬‭classes.‬‭We‬‭let‬‭the‬‭random‬‭target‬‭variable‬
‭be‬‭the‬‭label‬‭of‬‭the‬‭class,‬‭with‬
‭two‬ ‭options‬
‭or‬
‭.‬ ‭The‬ ‭distribution‬ ‭of‬ ‭the‬ ‭target‬ ‭variable‬ ‭is‬ ‭the‬ ‭Bernoulli‬

‭(2.9)‬
‭Where the success probability‬
‭depends on‬

‭If‬ ‭we‬‭consider‬‭a‬‭training‬‭set‬‭of‬‭independent‬‭observations‬
‭and‬‭try‬‭to‬‭approximate‬
‭with‬ ‭our‬ ‭neural‬ ‭network‬
