‭and‬
‭,‬ ‭respectively.‬ ‭However,‬ ‭only‬ ‭the‬
‭dropout-only‬‭model‬‭was‬‭found‬‭to‬‭perform‬‭significantly‬‭better‬‭than‬‭the‬‭model‬‭without‬‭dropout‬
‭37‬
==PAGE:42==
‭and‬ ‭weighting‬ ‭in‬ ‭terms‬ ‭of‬ ‭PPV‬ ‭(‬
‭)‬ ‭and‬ ‭AUC‬‭(‬
‭),‬‭as‬‭there‬‭was‬‭found‬‭no‬
‭significant‬ ‭difference‬ ‭between‬ ‭the‬ ‭weighting-only‬ ‭model‬ ‭and‬ ‭model‬ ‭without‬ ‭dropout‬ ‭and‬
‭weighting for these two metrics.‬
‭From‬ ‭the‬ ‭figures‬ ‭it‬ ‭is‬‭seen‬‭that‬‭dropout‬‭gives‬‭a‬‭larger‬‭performance‬‭boost‬‭than‬‭weighting.‬
‭However,‬‭the‬‭dropout-only‬‭model‬‭only‬‭significantly‬‭outperformed‬‭the‬‭weighting-only‬‭model‬‭in‬
‭terms‬ ‭of‬ ‭AUC‬ ‭(‬
‭),‬ ‭as‬ ‭there‬ ‭was‬ ‭found‬ ‭no‬ ‭significant‬ ‭difference‬ ‭between‬ ‭the‬‭two‬
‭models in terms of AUC 0.1 and PPV.‬
‭From‬ ‭the‬ ‭delta‬ ‭performance‬ ‭plots,‬ ‭we‬ ‭see‬ ‭that‬ ‭the‬ ‭increase‬ ‭in‬ ‭mean‬ ‭performance‬ ‭when‬
‭going‬‭from‬‭the‬‭model‬‭with‬‭no‬‭dropout‬‭and‬‭no‬‭weighting‬‭to‬‭the‬‭model‬‭with‬‭weighting‬‭only,‬‭is‬
‭consistently‬‭larger‬‭across‬‭all‬‭metrics‬‭than‬‭the‬‭increase‬‭in‬‭weighted‬‭mean‬‭performance.‬‭This‬
‭means‬‭that‬‭the‬‭performance‬‭gain‬‭is‬‭primarily‬‭seen‬‭for‬‭the‬‭least‬‭abundant‬‭peptides,‬‭which‬‭is‬
‭what‬‭we‬‭would‬‭expect,‬‭since‬‭weighting‬‭peptides‬‭with‬‭fewer‬‭observations‬‭higher‬‭in‬‭the‬‭loss‬
‭function should lead to greater performance for these peptides.‬
‭When‬‭going‬‭from‬‭the‬‭model‬‭with‬‭no‬‭dropout‬‭and‬‭no‬‭weighting‬‭to‬‭the‬‭model‬‭with‬‭dropout‬‭only,‬
‭the‬ ‭increase‬ ‭in‬ ‭unweighted‬ ‭mean‬ ‭performance‬ ‭is‬ ‭again‬ ‭consistently‬ ‭larger‬ ‭across‬ ‭all‬
‭performance‬‭measures,‬‭meaning‬‭that‬‭peptides‬‭with‬‭the‬‭least‬‭amount‬‭of‬‭observations‬‭have‬
‭the‬‭greatest‬‭increase‬‭in‬‭performance.‬‭This‬‭can‬‭be‬‭explained‬‭by‬‭the‬‭fact‬‭that‬‭with‬‭no‬‭dropout‬
‭the‬‭model‬‭tends‬‭to‬‭overfit‬‭more,‬‭especially‬‭to‬‭peptides‬‭it‬‭has‬‭seen‬‭the‬‭most.‬‭Adding‬‭dropout‬
‭means‬‭that‬‭the‬‭model‬‭can‬‭generalize‬‭better‬‭to‬‭peptides‬‭it‬‭has‬‭not‬‭seen‬‭that‬‭often,‬‭leading‬‭to‬
‭an increased performance for these peptides.‬
‭4.2 Compare Embeddings while Keeping Parameters Constant‬
‭From‬‭the‬‭reproduced‬‭results,‬‭it‬‭is‬‭clear‬‭that‬‭it‬‭is‬‭important‬‭to‬‭include‬‭dropout‬‭and‬‭weighting‬‭in‬
‭the‬‭model.‬‭Thus,‬‭the‬‭BLOSUM50-embedded‬‭model‬‭using‬‭dropout‬‭and‬‭weighting‬‭was‬‭now‬
‭used‬‭as‬‭a‬‭baseline‬‭model‬‭to‬‭investigate‬‭different‬‭embeddings‬‭for‬‭the‬‭CDR‬‭sequences,‬‭while‬
‭keeping‬ ‭all‬ ‭other‬ ‭parameters‬ ‭constant.‬ ‭The‬ ‭analyzed‬ ‭embeddings‬ ‭were‬ ‭ESM-1b,‬
‭ProtT5-XL-U50‬ ‭and‬ ‭ESM-2,‬ ‭with‬ ‭embedding‬ ‭dimension‬ ‭sizes‬ ‭of‬ ‭1280,‬ ‭1024‬ ‭and‬ ‭1280‬
‭respectively.‬‭The‬‭new‬‭embeddings‬‭are‬‭thus‬‭much‬‭larger‬‭than‬‭the‬‭BLOSUM50‬‭embedding,‬
‭which‬‭has‬‭an‬‭embedding‬‭dimension‬‭size‬‭of‬‭only‬‭20.‬‭The‬‭model‬‭IDs‬‭of‬‭the‬‭tested‬‭models‬‭are‬
‭1,‬‭36,‬‭55‬‭and‬‭92‬‭(refer‬‭to‬‭table‬‭3.1).‬‭The‬‭difference‬‭in‬‭test‬‭performance‬‭is‬‭plotted‬‭(fig.‬‭4.5,‬
‭B.5-6).‬
‭From‬ ‭the‬ ‭plots,‬ ‭it‬ ‭is‬ ‭clear‬ ‭that‬‭the‬‭ESM-1b‬‭model‬‭performed‬‭the‬‭worst.‬‭Both‬‭its‬‭weighted‬
‭mean‬‭and‬‭mean‬‭performance‬‭is‬‭the‬‭lowest‬‭across‬‭all‬‭three‬‭performance‬‭measures‬‭and‬‭it‬‭has‬
‭the‬‭lowest‬‭performance‬‭for‬‭almost‬‭all‬‭peptides.‬‭In‬‭fact‬‭all‬‭other‬‭three‬‭models‬‭demonstrated‬
‭significantly‬‭better‬‭performance‬‭for‬‭all‬‭three‬‭performance‬‭metrics.‬‭For‬‭the‬‭BLOSUM50‬‭model‬
‭the‬‭p-values‬‭were‬‭determined‬‭to‬
‭,‬
‭and‬
‭for‬‭AUC‬‭0.1,‬‭PPV‬‭and‬
‭AUC,‬‭respectively.‬‭For‬‭the‬‭ESM-2‬‭model‬‭the‬‭obtained‬‭p-values‬‭were‬
‭for‬‭both‬‭AUC‬
‭0.1‬‭and‬‭AUC‬‭and‬
‭for‬‭PPV.‬‭Finally,‬‭for‬‭the‬‭ProtT5-XL-U50‬‭model‬‭the‬‭p-values‬‭were‬
‭found to be‬
‭,‬
‭and‬
‭for AUC 0.1, PPV and AUC, respectively.‬
‭38‬
==PAGE:43==
‭The‬ ‭plots‬ ‭also‬ ‭indicate‬ ‭that‬ ‭the‬ ‭BLOSUM50,‬ ‭ProtT5-XL-U50,‬ ‭and‬ ‭ESM-2‬ ‭models‬ ‭exhibit‬
‭similar‬ ‭performance.‬ ‭Specifically,‬ ‭the‬ ‭performance‬ ‭of‬ ‭these‬ ‭models‬ ‭were‬ ‭found‬ ‭to‬ ‭not‬‭be‬
‭significantly different across all metrics.‬
‭Fig.‬ ‭4.5.‬‭Difference‬‭in‬‭test‬‭performance‬‭between‬‭initial‬‭version‬‭of‬‭models‬‭with‬‭new‬‭embeddings‬‭and‬‭the‬
‭baseline‬ ‭model‬ ‭measured‬ ‭by‬ ‭ΔAUC‬ ‭0.1.‬ ‭In‬ ‭the‬‭initial‬‭version‬‭of‬‭models‬‭with‬‭new‬‭embeddings‬‭only‬‭the‬‭CDR‬
‭embedding‬‭is‬‭different‬‭from‬‭the‬‭baseline‬‭BLOSUM50-embedded‬‭model.‬‭All‬‭other‬‭parameters‬‭are‬‭kept‬‭constant.‬
‭The‬ ‭embeddings‬ ‭of‬ ‭the‬ ‭new‬‭models‬‭are‬‭ESM-1b,‬‭ProtT5-XL-U50‬‭and‬‭ESM-2‬‭indicated‬‭by‬‭different‬‭colors.‬‭The‬
‭performance‬‭of‬‭the‬‭baseline‬‭model‬‭is‬‭used‬‭as‬‭the‬‭origin‬‭and‬‭the‬‭performance‬‭of‬‭the‬‭other‬‭three‬‭models‬‭are‬‭given‬
‭as‬ ‭ΔAUC‬ ‭0.1‬ ‭relative‬ ‭to‬ ‭this‬ ‭origin.‬ ‭The‬ ‭per‬ ‭peptide‬ ‭difference‬ ‭in‬ ‭performance‬ ‭is‬ ‭shown‬ ‭to‬ ‭the‬ ‭right,‬ ‭where‬
‭peptides‬‭are‬‭sorted‬‭from‬‭the‬‭most‬‭abundant‬‭peptide‬‭to‬‭the‬‭least‬‭abundant‬‭peptide‬‭only‬‭counting‬‭positive‬‭peptides.‬
‭The‬‭difference‬‭in‬‭mean‬‭and‬‭weighted‬‭mean‬‭performance‬‭taken‬‭over‬‭all‬‭peptides‬‭is‬‭shown‬‭to‬‭the‬‭left,‬‭where‬‭the‬
‭weighted‬‭mean‬‭performance‬‭weights‬‭peptides‬‭after‬‭their‬‭occurrence.‬‭Numbers‬‭in‬‭parentheses‬‭in‬‭labels‬‭along‬‭the‬
‭first axis are the occurrence of positive peptides in each group.‬
‭4.3 Investigate Impact of Scaling and Activation Function‬
‭When‬‭keeping‬‭the‬‭parameters‬‭constant,‬‭it‬‭was‬‭not‬‭possible‬‭to‬‭find‬‭a‬‭model‬‭with‬‭a‬‭different‬
‭embedding‬‭for‬‭the‬‭CDR‬‭sequences‬‭that‬‭had‬‭significantly‬‭improved‬‭performance‬‭compared‬‭to‬
‭the‬ ‭BLOSUM50‬ ‭model.‬ ‭In‬ ‭all‬ ‭of‬ ‭these‬ ‭models‬ ‭where‬ ‭parameters‬ ‭were‬ ‭kept‬‭constant‬‭the‬
‭tested‬ ‭CDR‬ ‭embeddings‬ ‭were‬ ‭scaled‬ ‭by‬ ‭a‬ ‭scaling‬ ‭factor‬ ‭of‬ ‭1/5‬ ‭and‬ ‭a‬ ‭ReLU‬ ‭activation‬
‭function‬‭was‬‭applied‬‭to‬‭the‬‭convolutional‬‭layer‬‭for‬‭CDRs.‬‭To‬‭further‬‭investigate‬‭if‬‭it‬‭is‬‭possible‬
‭to‬ ‭improve‬ ‭upon‬ ‭the‬ ‭baseline‬ ‭model,‬ ‭the‬ ‭previously‬ ‭tested‬ ‭embeddings‬ ‭were‬ ‭scaled‬ ‭by‬
‭different‬ ‭scaling‬ ‭factors‬ ‭and‬‭the‬‭sigmoid‬‭activation‬‭function‬‭was‬‭tried‬‭for‬‭the‬‭convolutional‬
‭layer‬‭for‬‭CDRs‬‭in‬‭addition‬‭to‬‭the‬‭ReLU‬‭activation‬‭function.‬‭This‬‭was‬‭done‬‭for‬‭the‬‭BLOSUM50‬
‭embedding‬ ‭as‬ ‭well‬ ‭in‬ ‭order‬ ‭to‬ ‭have‬ ‭a‬ ‭fair‬ ‭comparison.‬ ‭When‬‭ranking‬‭the‬‭models‬‭for‬‭the‬
‭different‬ ‭embeddings,‬ ‭the‬ ‭model‬ ‭performances‬ ‭were‬ ‭calculated‬‭on‬‭the‬‭validation‬‭set.‬‭It‬‭is‬
‭important‬‭that‬‭hyperparameters‬‭were‬‭not‬‭selected‬‭on‬‭the‬‭test‬‭set.‬‭If‬‭they‬‭were‬‭then‬‭using‬‭the‬
‭same‬ ‭test‬ ‭set‬ ‭to‬ ‭estimate‬‭the‬‭performance‬‭of‬‭the‬‭model‬‭with‬‭best‬‭hyperparameters‬‭could‬
‭39‬
==PAGE:44==
‭lead‬‭to‬‭performance‬‭overestimation.‬‭In‬‭fig.‬‭4.6,‬‭the‬‭AUC‬‭0.1‬‭for‬‭the‬‭BLOSUM50‬‭embedding‬
‭is‬‭shown.‬‭A‬‭box‬‭plot‬‭is‬‭made‬‭for‬‭different‬‭scaling‬‭factors‬‭and‬‭for‬‭the‬‭two‬‭activation‬‭functions.‬
‭Likewise‬‭in‬‭fig.‬‭4.7,‬‭the‬‭AUC‬‭0.1‬‭for‬‭the‬‭ESM-2‬‭embedding‬‭is‬‭shown.‬‭PPV‬‭and‬‭AUC‬‭can‬‭be‬
‭found for the two embeddings in fig. B.7-10.‬
‭For‬‭the‬‭BLOSUM50‬‭embedding‬‭there‬‭does‬‭not‬‭appear‬‭to‬‭be‬‭a‬‭clear‬‭best‬‭scaling‬‭factor‬‭or‬
‭activation‬‭function.‬‭However,‬‭there‬‭appears‬‭to‬‭be‬‭a‬‭decrease‬‭in‬‭both‬‭AUC‬‭0.1‬‭and‬‭PPV‬‭for‬
‭the‬‭sigmoid‬‭activation‬‭function‬‭when‬‭the‬‭scaling‬‭factor‬‭is‬‭1/20‬‭or‬‭below.‬‭This‬‭drop‬‭is‬‭not‬‭as‬
‭apparent‬‭for‬‭AUC.‬‭On‬‭multiple‬‭of‬‭the‬‭learning‬‭curves‬‭for‬‭the‬‭20‬‭cross-validation‬‭models,‬‭we‬
‭also‬ ‭see‬ ‭an‬ ‭increase‬ ‭in‬‭the‬‭number‬‭of‬‭epochs‬‭before‬‭learning‬‭begins‬‭when‬‭going‬‭from‬‭a‬
‭scaling‬‭factor‬‭of‬‭1/15‬‭to‬‭scaling‬‭factor‬‭of‬‭1/20‬‭and‬‭these‬‭plateaus‬‭with‬‭no‬‭learning‬‭become‬
‭worse‬‭as‬‭the‬‭scaling‬‭factor‬‭gets‬‭reduced‬‭further‬‭(see‬‭fig.‬‭C.1-5).‬‭At‬‭a‬‭scaling‬‭factor‬‭of‬‭1/40‬
‭some‬‭of‬‭the‬‭cross-validation‬‭models‬‭did‬‭not‬‭even‬‭start‬‭learning‬‭(fig.‬‭C.5),‬‭and‬‭the‬‭model‬‭for‬‭a‬
‭scaling‬‭factor‬‭of‬‭1/40‬‭is‬‭thus‬‭not‬‭included‬‭in‬‭fig‬‭4.6.‬‭Considering‬‭the‬‭decreased‬‭performance‬
‭and‬‭the‬‭increase‬‭in‬‭time‬‭it‬‭takes‬‭before‬‭the‬‭model‬‭starts‬‭to‬‭learn,‬‭the‬‭scaling‬‭factor‬‭for‬‭the‬
‭BLOSUM50‬ ‭encoding‬ ‭should‬ ‭be‬ ‭above‬ ‭1/20‬ ‭for‬ ‭the‬ ‭sigmoid‬ ‭activation‬ ‭function.‬ ‭It‬ ‭also‬
‭appears‬‭that‬‭the‬‭scaling‬‭factor‬‭should‬‭be‬‭below‬‭1‬‭for‬‭the‬‭sigmoid‬‭activation‬‭function‬‭since‬‭we‬
‭both‬ ‭have‬ ‭a‬ ‭lower‬ ‭AUC‬ ‭and‬ ‭AUC‬ ‭0.1‬ ‭at‬ ‭a‬ ‭scaling‬ ‭factor‬ ‭of‬ ‭1.‬ ‭For‬ ‭the‬ ‭ReLU‬ ‭activation‬
‭function,‬‭all‬‭the‬‭tested‬‭scaling‬‭factors‬‭performed‬‭equally‬‭well,‬‭except‬‭for‬‭a‬‭scaling‬‭factor‬‭of‬‭1.‬
‭At‬ ‭this‬ ‭scaling‬ ‭factor,‬ ‭none‬ ‭of‬ ‭the‬ ‭partitions‬ ‭started‬ ‭learning‬ ‭(fig.‬ ‭C.6).‬ ‭So‬ ‭for‬ ‭the‬ ‭ReLU‬
‭activation function, the scaling factor should be below 1.‬
‭For‬ ‭the‬ ‭ESM-2‬‭embedding,‬‭the‬‭sigmoid‬‭activation‬‭function‬‭clearly‬‭outperformed‬‭the‬‭ReLU‬
‭activation‬‭function‬‭(see‬‭fig‬‭4.7,‬‭B.9-10).‬‭For‬‭the‬‭sigmoid‬‭activation‬‭function,‬‭the‬‭performance‬
‭is‬‭clearly‬‭worse‬‭at‬‭a‬‭scaling‬‭factor‬‭of‬‭1‬‭across‬‭all‬‭metrics,‬‭and‬‭a‬‭drop‬‭in‬‭AUC‬‭0.1‬‭is‬‭observed‬
‭at‬‭a‬‭scaling‬‭factor‬‭of‬‭1/30.‬‭Since‬‭we‬‭see‬‭an‬‭increase‬‭in‬‭the‬‭number‬‭of‬‭epochs‬‭before‬‭the‬
‭cross-validation‬‭models‬‭start‬‭learning‬‭at‬‭a‬‭scaling‬‭factor‬‭of‬‭1/30‬‭and‬‭below,‬‭with‬‭multiple‬‭of‬
‭the‬‭cross-validation‬‭models‬‭not‬‭learning‬‭at‬‭a‬‭scaling‬‭factor‬‭of‬‭1/40,‬‭the‬‭scaling‬‭factor‬‭should‬
‭be‬‭above‬‭1/30‬‭for‬‭the‬‭sigmoid‬‭activation‬‭function.‬‭For‬‭the‬‭ReLU‬‭activation‬‭function,‬‭we‬‭see‬‭a‬
‭clear‬‭drop‬‭in‬‭AUC‬‭0.1‬‭and‬‭PPV‬‭at‬‭a‬‭scaling‬‭factor‬‭of‬‭1/10‬‭and‬‭above‬‭with‬‭no‬‭learning‬‭at‬‭a‬
‭scaling‬‭factor‬‭of‬‭1.‬‭For‬‭AUC‬‭the‬‭drop‬‭appears‬‭at‬‭a‬‭scaling‬‭factor‬‭of‬‭1/5.‬‭This‬‭indicates‬‭that‬
‭the scaling factor for ReLU should be below 1/10.‬
‭The‬‭same‬‭figures‬‭were‬‭made‬‭for‬‭the‬‭ESM-1b‬‭and‬‭ProtT5-XL-U50‬‭embedding‬‭(fig.‬‭B.11-16).‬
‭In‬ ‭both‬ ‭cases,‬ ‭the‬ ‭sigmoid‬ ‭activation‬ ‭function‬ ‭performed‬ ‭distinctly‬ ‭better‬ ‭than‬ ‭the‬ ‭ReLU‬
‭activation‬ ‭function.‬ ‭Having‬ ‭chosen‬ ‭the‬ ‭sigmoid‬ ‭activation‬‭function,‬‭it‬‭was‬‭assessed‬‭in‬‭the‬
‭same‬‭way‬‭as‬‭for‬‭the‬‭BLOSUM50‬‭and‬‭ESM-2‬‭model‬‭that‬‭the‬‭best‬‭ESM-1b‬‭model‬‭should‬‭be‬
‭found‬‭for‬‭a‬‭scaling‬‭factor‬‭below‬‭1‬‭and‬‭above‬‭1/40.‬‭For‬‭the‬‭ProtT5-XL-U50‬‭embedding‬‭the‬
‭scaling factor should be below 1 and above 1/30.‬
‭For‬‭both‬‭of‬‭these‬‭embeddings‬‭the‬‭behavior‬‭of‬‭the‬‭learning‬‭curves‬‭was‬‭similar‬‭to‬‭what‬‭was‬
‭seen‬‭for‬‭the‬‭BLOSUM50‬‭and‬‭ESM-2‬‭embedding.‬‭This‬‭means‬‭no‬‭learning‬‭for‬‭multiple‬‭or‬‭all‬‭of‬
‭the‬‭cross-validation‬‭models‬‭when‬‭using‬‭the‬‭ReLU‬‭function‬‭and‬‭selecting‬‭a‬‭scaling‬‭value‬‭of‬‭1.‬
‭This‬‭also‬‭means‬‭plateaus‬‭in‬‭the‬‭start‬‭of‬‭the‬‭learning‬‭curves‬‭for‬‭small‬‭scaling‬‭factors‬‭when‬
‭applying‬‭the‬‭sigmoid‬‭function‬‭with‬‭worse‬‭plateaus‬‭as‬‭the‬‭scaling‬‭factor‬‭gets‬‭reduced.‬‭For‬‭the‬
‭ESM-1b‬‭embedding‬‭the‬‭model‬‭with‬‭scaling‬‭factors‬‭of‬‭1/50‬‭failed‬‭to‬‭start‬‭learning‬‭for‬‭multiple‬
‭of‬‭its‬‭cross-validation‬‭models,‬‭while‬‭for‬‭the‬‭ProtT5-XL-U50‬‭embedding‬‭models‬‭with‬‭scaling‬
‭factors of 1/40 and 1/50 failed.‬
‭40‬
==PAGE:45==
‭For‬ ‭all‬ ‭four‬ ‭embeddings‬ ‭almost‬ ‭no‬ ‭plateaus‬ ‭were‬ ‭found‬ ‭for‬ ‭the‬ ‭ReLU‬ ‭function,‬ ‭the‬ ‭only‬
‭exception‬‭being‬‭when‬‭a‬‭scaling‬‭factor‬‭of‬‭1‬‭was‬‭used,‬‭which‬‭caused‬‭either‬‭no‬‭learning‬‭for‬‭all‬
‭of‬ ‭the‬ ‭20‬ ‭cross-validation‬‭models‬‭(fig.‬‭C.6)‬‭or‬‭that‬‭a‬‭few‬‭cross-validation‬‭models‬‭did‬‭start‬
‭learning‬ ‭but‬ ‭only‬ ‭after‬ ‭some‬ ‭duration‬ ‭of‬ ‭no‬ ‭learning‬ ‭(fig.‬ ‭C.7).‬ ‭For‬ ‭the‬ ‭ESM-1b‬ ‭model,‬
‭plateaus also occurred with a scaling factor of 1/5 (fig. C.8).‬
‭Fig.‬‭4.6.‬‭Effect‬‭of‬‭scaling‬‭and‬‭activation‬‭function‬‭on‬‭validation‬‭performance‬‭of‬‭the‬‭BLOSUM50‬‭embedded‬
‭model‬‭measured‬‭by‬‭AUC‬‭0.1.‬‭Two‬‭activation‬‭functions‬‭were‬‭tested;‬‭sigmoid‬‭and‬‭ReLU,‬‭and‬‭they‬‭are‬‭shown‬‭by‬
‭different‬‭colors.‬‭Different‬‭tested‬‭scaling‬‭factors‬‭are‬‭shown‬‭along‬‭the‬‭first‬‭axis.‬‭Boxplots‬‭summarize‬‭the‬‭distribution‬
‭of‬‭the‬‭performance‬‭of‬‭20‬‭cross-validation‬‭models.‬‭Whiskers‬‭extend‬‭to‬‭the‬‭largest/smallest‬‭performance‬‭no‬‭further‬
‭than‬‭a‬‭distance‬‭of‬
‭from‬‭the‬‭hinge.‬‭Outliers‬‭are‬‭defined‬‭as‬‭values‬‭with‬‭a‬‭distance‬‭greater‬‭than‬
‭1‬. ‭5‬ · ‭𝐼𝑄𝑅‬

‭from‬‭the‬‭hinge‬‭and‬‭are‬‭shown‬‭as‬‭circles.‬‭The‬‭averages‬‭taken‬‭over‬‭the‬‭20‬‭cross-validation‬‭models‬‭are‬‭shown‬‭as‬

‭4.4 Compare Embeddings for Found Scaling and Activation‬
‭Function‬
‭The‬‭embeddings‬‭were‬‭now‬‭compared‬‭for‬‭optimal‬‭scaling‬‭factor‬‭and‬‭activation‬‭function.‬‭For‬
‭the‬‭BLOSUM50‬‭embedding,‬‭the‬‭ReLU‬‭activation‬‭function‬‭was‬‭chosen‬‭with‬‭a‬‭scaling‬‭factor‬‭of‬
‭1/5.‬‭For‬‭the‬‭remaining‬‭embeddings,‬‭the‬‭sigmoid‬‭activation‬‭function‬‭with‬‭a‬‭scaling‬‭factor‬‭of‬
‭1/20‬‭was‬‭chosen.‬‭The‬‭difference‬‭in‬‭test‬‭performance‬‭between‬‭the‬‭embeddings‬‭is‬‭plotted‬‭(fig.‬
‭4.8, B.17-18).‬
‭From‬ ‭the‬ ‭plots,‬ ‭it‬ ‭is‬ ‭clear‬ ‭that‬ ‭the‬ ‭baseline‬ ‭model‬ ‭using‬ ‭the‬ ‭BLOSUM50‬ ‭embedding‬
‭performed‬ ‭the‬ ‭worst‬ ‭across‬ ‭all‬ ‭performance‬ ‭metrics.‬ ‭Specifically,‬ ‭all‬ ‭three‬ ‭models‬ ‭with‬
‭embeddings‬‭produced‬‭by‬‭transformers‬‭outperformed‬‭the‬‭BLOSUM50‬‭model‬‭significantly‬‭for‬
‭all‬‭three‬‭performance‬‭metrics.‬‭The‬‭ESM-1b‬‭model‬‭achieved‬‭p-values‬‭of‬
‭,‬
‭and‬
‭for‬‭AUC‬‭0.1,‬‭PPV‬‭and‬‭AUC,‬‭respectively.‬‭The‬‭p-values‬‭for‬‭the‬‭ESM-2‬‭model‬
‭were‬
‭for‬‭PPV‬‭and‬
‭for‬‭AUC‬‭0.1‬‭and‬‭AUC.‬‭Finally,‬‭for‬‭the‬‭ProtT5-XL-U50‬
‭model‬‭the‬‭following‬‭p-values‬‭were‬‭obtained;‬
‭for‬‭PPV‬‭and‬
‭for‬‭AUC‬‭0.1‬
‭and AUC.‬
‭42‬
==PAGE:47==
‭When‬ ‭looking‬ ‭at‬ ‭the‬ ‭plots,‬ ‭the‬ ‭remaining‬ ‭three‬ ‭embeddings‬ ‭were‬ ‭found‬ ‭to‬ ‭have‬ ‭similar‬
‭performance.‬ ‭However,‬ ‭the‬ ‭ESM-2‬ ‭model‬‭seemed‬‭to‬‭perform‬‭a‬‭little‬‭better‬‭than‬‭the‬‭other‬
‭two,‬‭since‬‭we‬‭see‬‭a‬‭higher‬‭mean‬‭and‬‭weighted‬‭mean‬‭AUC‬‭0.1‬‭and‬‭PPV‬‭compared‬‭to‬‭the‬
‭other‬‭two‬‭models.‬‭The‬‭weighted‬‭mean‬‭AUC‬‭is‬‭also‬‭higher.‬‭It‬‭is‬‭only‬‭the‬‭mean‬‭AUC‬‭that‬‭is‬‭a‬
‭little‬‭lower‬‭than‬‭for‬‭the‬‭other‬‭two‬‭models.‬‭The‬‭ESM-1b‬‭model‬‭comes‬‭second‬‭with‬‭a‬‭higher‬
‭mean‬‭and‬‭weighted‬‭mean‬‭PPV‬‭and‬‭AUC‬‭0.1‬‭compared‬‭to‬‭the‬‭ProtT5-XL-U50‬‭model.‬‭The‬
‭mean and weighted mean AUC is however a little lower.‬
‭When‬ ‭doing‬ ‭statistical‬ ‭hypothesis‬ ‭testing‬ ‭there‬ ‭was‬ ‭however‬ ‭not‬ ‭found‬ ‭any‬ ‭significant‬
‭difference between the three models, across all metrics.‬
‭Fig.‬‭4.8.‬‭Difference‬‭in‬‭test‬‭performance‬‭between‬‭second‬‭version‬‭of‬‭models‬‭with‬‭new‬‭embeddings‬‭and‬‭the‬
‭baseline‬ ‭model‬ ‭measured‬ ‭by‬ ‭ΔAUC‬ ‭0.1.‬ ‭In‬ ‭the‬ ‭second‬ ‭version‬ ‭of‬‭models‬‭with‬‭new‬‭embeddings‬‭the‬‭scaling‬
‭factor‬‭has‬‭been‬‭optimized‬‭to‬‭a‬‭value‬‭of‬‭1/20‬‭and‬‭the‬‭sigmoid‬‭activation‬‭function‬‭is‬‭used‬‭on‬‭the‬‭convolutional‬‭layer‬
‭for‬‭CDRs‬‭instead‬‭of‬‭ReLU.‬‭The‬‭embeddings‬‭of‬‭the‬‭models‬‭are‬‭ESM-1b,‬‭ProtT5-XL-U50‬‭and‬‭ESM-2‬‭indicated‬‭by‬
‭different‬ ‭colors.‬ ‭The‬ ‭performance‬ ‭of‬ ‭the‬ ‭baseline‬ ‭BLOSUM50-embedded‬ ‭model‬ ‭is‬ ‭used‬ ‭as‬ ‭the‬ ‭origin‬‭and‬‭the‬
‭performance‬‭of‬‭the‬‭other‬‭three‬‭models‬‭are‬‭given‬‭as‬‭ΔAUC‬‭0.1‬‭relative‬‭to‬‭this‬‭origin.‬‭The‬‭per‬‭peptide‬‭difference‬‭in‬
‭performance‬ ‭is‬ ‭shown‬ ‭to‬ ‭the‬ ‭right,‬ ‭where‬ ‭peptides‬ ‭are‬ ‭sorted‬ ‭from‬ ‭the‬ ‭most‬ ‭abundant‬ ‭peptide‬ ‭to‬ ‭the‬ ‭least‬
‭abundant‬‭peptide‬‭only‬‭counting‬‭positive‬‭peptides.‬‭The‬‭difference‬‭in‬‭mean‬‭and‬‭weighted‬‭mean‬‭performance‬‭taken‬
‭over‬ ‭all‬ ‭peptides‬ ‭is‬ ‭shown‬ ‭to‬ ‭the‬ ‭left,‬ ‭where‬ ‭the‬ ‭weighted‬ ‭mean‬ ‭performance‬ ‭weights‬ ‭peptides‬ ‭after‬ ‭their‬
‭occurrence.‬‭Numbers‬‭in‬‭parentheses‬‭in‬‭labels‬‭along‬‭the‬‭first‬‭axis‬‭are‬‭the‬‭occurrence‬‭of‬‭positive‬‭peptides‬‭in‬‭each‬
‭group.‬
‭4.5 Investigate whether Simpler FNN Model can Achieve‬
‭Similar Performance‬
‭It‬‭was‬‭now‬‭investigated‬‭if‬‭a‬‭simpler‬‭feedforward‬‭neural‬‭network‬‭(FNN)‬‭model‬‭could‬‭achieve‬
‭similar‬‭or‬‭better‬‭performance‬‭than‬‭the‬‭more‬‭complex‬‭CNN‬‭model.‬‭The‬‭assessment‬‭was‬‭done‬
‭for‬‭the‬‭ESM-1b‬‭embedding‬‭with‬‭a‬‭scaling‬‭factor‬‭of‬‭1/20‬‭and‬‭the‬‭sigmoid‬‭activation‬‭function.‬
‭43‬
==PAGE:48==
‭Other‬‭parameters‬‭such‬‭as‬‭number‬‭of‬‭hidden‬‭units,‬‭learning‬‭rate‬‭and‬‭dropout‬‭rate‬‭were‬‭also‬
‭kept the same for the simpler FNN model as for the CNN model.‬
‭For‬ ‭the‬ ‭CNN‬ ‭models‬ ‭the‬ ‭TCR‬ ‭sequences‬ ‭were‬ ‭embedded‬ ‭into‬ ‭matrix‬ ‭representations‬‭of‬
‭each‬ ‭CDR‬ ‭component‬ ‭with‬ ‭vector‬ ‭embeddings‬ ‭per‬ ‭amino‬ ‭acid.‬ ‭To‬ ‭make‬ ‭the‬ ‭ESM-1b‬
‭embedding‬‭compatible‬‭with‬‭the‬‭FNN‬‭it‬‭was‬‭made‬‭into‬‭vector‬‭representations‬‭of‬‭each‬‭CDR‬
‭component‬ ‭by‬ ‭taking‬ ‭the‬ ‭average‬ ‭over‬ ‭the‬ ‭amino‬ ‭acid‬ ‭vector‬ ‭embeddings‬ ‭in‬ ‭the‬ ‭matrix‬
‭representation‬‭of‬‭a‬‭CDR‬‭component.‬‭The‬‭peptide‬‭sequences‬‭which‬‭have‬‭also‬‭been‬‭matrix‬
‭representations‬‭in‬‭the‬‭CNN‬‭models‬‭were‬‭converted‬‭into‬‭vector‬‭representations‬‭by‬‭collapsing‬
‭the‬‭embeddings‬‭into‬‭one‬‭dimension.‬‭This‬‭was‬‭chosen‬‭over‬‭taking‬‭the‬‭average‬‭of‬‭the‬‭amino‬
‭acid‬ ‭vector‬ ‭embeddings‬ ‭inside‬ ‭to‬ ‭avoid‬ ‭that‬ ‭the‬ ‭information‬ ‭from‬ ‭the‬ ‭CDRs‬ ‭would‬
‭overshadow‬‭the‬‭information‬‭from‬‭the‬‭peptides.‬‭This‬‭was‬‭a‬‭concern‬‭due‬‭to‬‭the‬‭peptides‬‭being‬
‭embedded‬ ‭by‬ ‭BLOSUM50‬‭and‬‭thus‬‭having‬‭much‬‭smaller‬‭embedding‬‭dimension‬‭size‬‭than‬
‭the CDR embeddings.‬
‭Due‬‭to‬‭the‬‭lower‬‭complexity‬‭of‬‭the‬‭FNN‬‭model,‬‭it‬‭was‬‭speculated‬‭that‬‭keeping‬‭a‬‭high‬‭dropout‬
‭rate‬ ‭in‬ ‭the‬ ‭simple‬ ‭model‬ ‭would‬‭result‬‭in‬‭too‬‭much‬‭information‬‭loss‬‭for‬‭the‬‭model‬‭to‬‭learn‬
‭properly. A model where the dropout rate was set to zero was therefore also tested.‬
‭First‬ ‭the‬ ‭two‬ ‭FNN‬ ‭models‬ ‭were‬ ‭ranked‬ ‭based‬ ‭on‬ ‭their‬ ‭performance‬ ‭calculated‬ ‭on‬ ‭the‬
‭validation‬‭set‬‭(fig.‬‭4.9,‬‭B.19-20).‬‭For‬‭all‬‭three‬‭performance‬‭measures,‬‭the‬‭model‬‭with‬‭dropout‬
‭has‬‭a‬‭higher‬‭mean‬‭performance,‬‭and‬‭thus‬‭appears‬‭to‬‭be‬‭the‬‭better‬‭model.‬‭Thus‬‭the‬‭simpler‬
‭model with dropout was selected.‬
‭The‬ ‭performance‬ ‭of‬ ‭this‬ ‭FNN‬‭model‬‭calculated‬‭on‬‭the‬‭test‬‭set‬‭was‬‭now‬‭compared‬‭to‬‭the‬
‭performance‬‭of‬‭the‬‭CNN‬‭model‬‭(fig‬‭4.10,‬‭B.21-22).‬‭From‬‭the‬‭plots‬‭we‬‭see‬‭that‬‭the‬‭simpler‬
‭model‬‭has‬‭lower‬‭mean‬‭and‬‭weighted‬‭mean‬‭performance‬‭across‬‭all‬‭performance‬‭measures,‬
‭and‬‭that‬‭the‬‭performance‬‭per‬‭peptide‬‭is‬‭also‬‭lower‬‭for‬‭most‬‭of‬‭the‬‭peptides.‬‭From‬‭statistical‬
‭hypothesis‬‭testing‬‭it‬‭is‬‭found‬‭that‬‭the‬‭CNN‬‭model‬‭performs‬‭significantly‬‭better‬‭than‬‭the‬‭FNN‬
‭model‬ ‭for‬ ‭AUC‬‭0.1‬‭(‬
‭)‬‭and‬‭AUC‬‭(‬
‭),‬‭but‬‭not‬‭in‬‭terms‬‭of‬‭PPV‬‭(‬
‭).‬
‭Despite‬ ‭there‬ ‭being‬ ‭no‬ ‭significant‬ ‭difference‬ ‭between‬ ‭the‬ ‭two‬ ‭models‬ ‭in‬ ‭terms‬ ‭of‬‭PPV‬‭it‬
‭seems‬‭like‬‭that‬‭a‬‭simpler‬‭FNN‬‭will‬‭not‬‭perform‬‭as‬‭well‬‭as‬‭the‬‭more‬‭complex‬‭CNN.‬‭Therefore‬
‭no more experiments were done for the simpler FNN.‬

‭shown as crosses.‬

‭measured‬‭by‬‭ΔAUC‬‭0.1.‬‭The‬‭FNN‬‭model‬‭is‬‭the‬‭one‬‭with‬‭dropout.‬‭The‬‭performance‬‭of‬‭the‬‭CNN‬‭model‬‭is‬‭used‬‭as‬
‭the‬ ‭origin‬ ‭and‬ ‭the‬ ‭performance‬ ‭of‬ ‭the‬‭FNN‬‭model‬‭is‬‭given‬‭as‬‭ΔAUC‬‭0.1‬‭relative‬‭to‬‭this‬‭origin.‬‭The‬‭per‬‭peptide‬
‭difference‬‭in‬‭performance‬‭is‬‭shown‬‭to‬‭the‬‭right,‬‭where‬‭peptides‬‭are‬‭sorted‬‭from‬‭the‬‭most‬‭abundant‬‭peptide‬‭to‬‭the‬
‭least‬‭abundant‬‭peptide‬‭only‬‭counting‬‭positive‬‭peptides.‬‭The‬‭difference‬‭in‬‭mean‬‭and‬‭weighted‬‭mean‬‭performance‬
‭taken‬ ‭over‬ ‭all‬ ‭peptides‬‭is‬‭shown‬‭to‬‭the‬‭left,‬‭where‬‭the‬‭weighted‬‭mean‬‭performance‬‭weights‬‭peptides‬‭after‬‭their‬
‭occurrence.‬‭Numbers‬‭in‬‭parentheses‬‭in‬‭labels‬‭along‬‭the‬‭first‬‭axis‬‭are‬‭the‬‭occurrence‬‭of‬‭positive‬‭peptides‬‭in‬‭each‬
‭group.‬

==PAGE:50==
‭4.6 Investigate Impact of Architecture Size‬
‭Since‬ ‭the‬ ‭ESM-1b,‬ ‭ProtT5-XL-U50‬ ‭and‬ ‭ESM-2‬ ‭embedding‬ ‭are‬ ‭all‬ ‭much‬ ‭larger‬ ‭than‬ ‭the‬
‭BLOSUM50‬ ‭embedding‬ ‭and‬ ‭potentially‬ ‭have‬ ‭more‬ ‭information‬ ‭stored‬ ‭inside,‬ ‭it‬ ‭was‬
‭speculated‬ ‭that‬ ‭they‬ ‭would‬ ‭benefit‬ ‭from‬‭a‬‭larger‬‭NetTCR‬‭architecture‬‭size‬‭to‬‭process‬‭the‬
‭information.‬‭Therefore,‬‭new‬‭2X‬‭CNN‬‭models‬‭were‬‭made‬‭with‬‭double‬‭the‬‭number‬‭of‬‭hidden‬
‭units‬‭and‬‭convolution‬‭filters.‬‭First‬‭the‬‭validation‬‭performance‬‭for‬‭the‬‭1X‬‭and‬‭2X‬‭version‬‭of‬
‭ESM-1b‬ ‭model‬ ‭were‬ ‭compared‬ ‭for‬ ‭different‬ ‭values‬ ‭of‬‭scaling‬‭and‬‭for‬‭both‬‭the‬‭ReLU‬‭and‬
‭sigmoid activation function (fig. 4.11, B.23-24).‬
‭From‬‭the‬‭figures,‬‭it‬‭is‬‭apparent‬‭that‬‭the‬‭sigmoid‬‭activation‬‭function‬‭performed‬‭the‬‭best‬‭for‬‭the‬
‭2X‬‭model,‬‭just‬‭as‬‭for‬‭the‬‭1X‬‭model.‬‭Also,‬‭the‬‭maximum‬‭mean‬‭performance‬‭is‬‭higher‬‭for‬‭the‬
‭2X‬ ‭model‬ ‭than‬ ‭for‬ ‭the‬ ‭1X‬ ‭model‬‭for‬‭both‬‭activation‬‭functions‬‭and‬‭across‬‭all‬‭performance‬
‭measures.‬ ‭Thus,‬ ‭it‬ ‭looks‬ ‭like‬ ‭we‬ ‭can‬ ‭gain‬ ‭an‬ ‭increase‬ ‭in‬ ‭performance‬ ‭by‬ ‭doubling‬ ‭the‬
‭architecture size.‬
‭When‬‭looking‬‭at‬‭the‬‭performance‬‭of‬‭models‬‭for‬‭the‬‭ReLU‬‭function,‬‭we‬‭see‬‭that‬‭the‬‭window‬‭of‬
‭best‬‭performing‬‭models‬‭across‬‭different‬‭scaling‬‭factors‬‭is‬‭much‬‭smaller‬‭for‬‭the‬‭2X‬‭models‬
‭than‬‭for‬‭the‬‭1X‬‭models,‬‭and‬‭we‬‭see‬‭a‬‭vast‬‭decrease‬‭in‬‭performance‬‭when‬‭decreasing‬‭the‬
‭scaling‬‭factor‬‭from‬‭1/25‬‭and‬‭below.‬‭As‬‭was‬‭the‬‭case‬‭for‬‭the‬‭1X‬‭models‬‭using‬‭a‬‭scaling‬‭factor‬
‭of 1 results in a failed model.‬
‭For‬‭the‬‭sigmoid‬‭activation‬‭function,‬‭there‬‭are‬‭only‬‭two‬‭scaling‬‭factors‬‭(1/5‬‭and‬‭1/10)‬‭where‬‭all‬
‭cross-validation‬‭models‬‭started‬‭learning.‬‭For‬‭the‬‭scaling‬‭factors‬‭1,‬‭1/15,‬‭1/20,‬‭1/25‬‭and‬‭1/30,‬
‭multiple‬‭of‬‭the‬‭cross-validation‬‭models‬ ‭did‬‭not‬‭start‬‭learning,‬‭and‬‭for‬‭a‬‭scaling‬‭factor‬‭of‬‭1/40,‬
‭none of the cross-validation models started learning.‬
‭As‬‭was‬‭the‬‭case‬‭for‬‭the‬‭1X‬‭sigmoid‬‭models,‬‭the‬‭2X‬‭ESM-1b‬‭sigmoid‬‭models‬‭experienced‬
‭plateaus‬ ‭at‬ ‭the‬ ‭beginning‬ ‭of‬ ‭the‬ ‭learning‬ ‭curves.‬ ‭However,‬ ‭this‬ ‭time‬ ‭the‬ ‭plateaus‬ ‭had‬
‭become‬‭much‬‭worse,‬‭now‬‭happening‬‭for‬‭all‬‭tested‬‭scaling‬‭factors‬‭except‬‭for‬‭a‬‭scaling‬‭factor‬
‭of‬‭1/5.‬‭The‬‭duration‬‭of‬‭the‬‭plateaus‬‭had‬‭also‬‭generally‬‭become‬‭longer‬‭(compare‬‭fig.‬‭C.9‬‭with‬
‭C.10‬‭and‬‭C.11‬‭with‬‭C.12).‬‭As‬‭for‬‭the‬‭1X‬‭sigmoid‬‭models‬‭the‬‭plateaus‬‭were‬‭worse‬‭for‬‭smaller‬
‭scaling‬ ‭factors,‬ ‭eventually‬ ‭resulting‬ ‭in‬ ‭that‬ ‭none‬ ‭of‬ ‭the‬ ‭cross-validation‬ ‭models‬ ‭started‬
‭learning at a scaling factor of 1/40.‬
‭46‬
==PAGE:51==
‭Fig.‬‭4.11.‬‭Effect‬‭of‬‭architecture‬‭size‬‭on‬‭validation‬‭performance‬‭of‬‭the‬‭ESM-1b‬‭embedded‬‭model‬‭measured‬
‭by‬‭AUC‬‭0.1.‬‭Two‬‭architecture‬‭sizes‬‭shown‬‭by‬‭different‬‭colors‬‭were‬‭tested;‬‭1X‬‭and‬‭2X.‬‭The‬‭2X‬‭model‬‭has‬‭double‬
‭the‬‭amount‬‭of‬‭hidden‬‭units‬‭and‬‭convolution‬‭filters‬‭as‬‭the‬‭1X‬‭model.‬‭The‬‭test‬‭was‬‭done‬‭for‬‭two‬‭activation‬‭functions;‬
‭sigmoid‬ ‭and‬ ‭ReLU‬ ‭shown‬ ‭as‬ ‭different‬ ‭facets.‬ ‭Different‬ ‭tested‬ ‭scaling‬ ‭factors‬ ‭are‬ ‭shown‬ ‭along‬ ‭the‬ ‭first‬ ‭axis.‬
‭Boxplots‬ ‭summarize‬ ‭the‬ ‭distribution‬ ‭of‬ ‭the‬ ‭performance‬ ‭of‬ ‭20‬ ‭cross-validation‬‭models.‬‭Whiskers‬‭extend‬‭to‬‭the‬
‭largest/smallest‬ ‭performance‬ ‭no‬ ‭further‬ ‭than‬ ‭a‬ ‭distance‬ ‭of‬
‭from‬ ‭the‬ ‭hinge.‬ ‭Outliers‬ ‭are‬ ‭defined‬ ‭as‬
‭1‬. ‭5‬ · ‭𝐼𝑄𝑅‬
‭values‬‭with‬‭a‬‭distance‬‭greater‬‭than‬
‭from‬‭the‬‭hinge‬‭and‬‭are‬‭shown‬‭as‬‭circles.‬‭The‬‭averages‬‭taken‬‭over‬
‭1‬. ‭5‬ · ‭𝐼𝑄𝑅‬
‭the 20 cross-validation models are shown as crosses.‬
‭It‬‭was‬‭hypothesized‬‭that‬‭the‬‭learning‬‭rate‬‭was‬‭too‬‭large‬‭for‬‭the‬‭more‬‭complex‬‭2X‬‭models,‬
‭and‬‭therefore‬‭new‬‭2X‬‭models‬‭were‬‭tested‬‭with‬‭half‬‭the‬‭learning‬‭rate‬‭(0.0005).‬‭This‬‭was‬‭only‬
‭done‬‭for‬‭the‬‭sigmoid‬‭function,‬‭since‬‭it‬‭so‬‭far‬‭has‬‭produced‬‭better‬‭results‬‭compared‬‭to‬‭the‬
‭ReLU activation function.‬
‭In‬‭fig.‬‭4.12‬‭and‬‭B.25-26,‬‭the‬‭2X‬‭ESM-1b‬‭model‬‭with‬‭half‬‭learning‬‭rate‬‭is‬‭compared‬‭with‬‭the‬
‭2X and 1X models with the original learning rate (0.001).‬
‭At‬‭half‬‭learning‬‭rate,‬‭the‬‭2X‬‭model‬‭now‬‭starts‬‭learning‬‭for‬‭all‬‭cross-validation‬‭models‬‭for‬‭all‬
‭tested‬ ‭scaling‬ ‭factors,‬ ‭where‬ ‭the‬ ‭previous‬ ‭2X‬ ‭model‬ ‭failed.‬ ‭We‬ ‭see‬ ‭an‬ ‭improvement‬ ‭in‬
‭performance‬‭across‬‭all‬‭performance‬‭measures‬‭compared‬‭to‬‭the‬‭previous‬‭2X‬‭models‬‭(scaling‬
‭factors‬‭1/5‬‭and‬‭1/10).‬‭We‬‭also‬‭generally‬‭see‬‭an‬‭increase‬‭in‬‭performance‬‭over‬‭the‬‭1X‬‭model‬
‭across performance measures and scaling factors.‬
‭Comparing‬‭the‬‭learning‬‭curves‬‭for‬‭the‬‭2X‬‭ESM-1b‬‭models‬‭with‬‭half‬‭learning‬‭rate‬‭and‬‭original‬
‭learning‬ ‭rate,‬ ‭it‬ ‭is‬ ‭observed‬ ‭that‬ ‭the‬ ‭plateaus‬ ‭are‬ ‭mostly‬ ‭gone‬ ‭for‬ ‭the‬ ‭models‬ ‭with‬ ‭half‬
‭learning‬‭rate,‬‭now‬‭only‬‭occurring‬‭to‬‭a‬‭small‬‭degree‬‭for‬‭the‬‭smallest‬‭scaling‬‭factors‬‭(compare‬
‭fig. C.9 with C.13 and C.11 with C.14).‬
‭47‬
==PAGE:52==
‭Looking‬‭at‬‭the‬‭validation‬‭performance‬‭plots‬‭for‬‭the‬‭ESM-1b‬‭model‬‭(fig.‬‭4.12‬‭and‬‭B.25-26)‬‭it‬‭is‬
‭not‬‭that‬‭obvious‬‭which‬‭scaling‬‭factor‬‭for‬‭the‬‭2X‬‭architecture‬‭with‬‭half‬‭learning‬‭rate‬‭results‬‭in‬
‭the‬ ‭highest‬‭performance,‬‭but‬‭a‬‭scaling‬‭factor‬‭of‬‭1/5‬‭seems‬‭optimal‬‭with‬‭1/10‬‭coming‬‭right‬
‭after.‬‭At‬‭a‬‭scaling‬‭factor‬‭of‬‭1/5,‬‭both‬‭mean‬‭AUC‬‭0.1‬‭and‬‭mean‬‭PPV‬‭is‬‭highest,‬‭whereas‬‭the‬
‭mean‬‭AUC‬‭is‬‭highest‬‭at‬‭a‬‭scaling‬‭factor‬‭of‬‭1/10.‬‭This‬‭also‬‭agrees‬‭with‬‭the‬‭ranking‬‭of‬‭the‬‭test‬
‭performances‬ ‭(not‬ ‭shown)‬ ‭with‬ ‭a‬ ‭scaling‬ ‭factor‬ ‭of‬ ‭1/5‬ ‭ranking‬ ‭highest‬ ‭for‬ ‭all‬ ‭mean‬ ‭and‬
‭weighted‬‭mean‬‭performance‬‭measures‬‭and‬‭a‬‭scaling‬‭factor‬‭of‬‭1/10‬‭ranking‬‭second‬‭highest‬
‭for all mean and weighted mean performance measures except weighted mean PPV.‬
‭2X‬‭models‬‭with‬‭half‬‭learning‬‭rate‬‭were‬‭also‬‭investigated‬‭for‬‭the‬‭ProtT5-XL-U50‬‭and‬‭ESM-2‬
‭embeddings.‬‭All‬‭of‬‭the‬‭tested‬‭scaling‬‭factors‬‭resulted‬‭in‬‭models‬‭that‬‭started‬‭learning‬‭even‬‭for‬
‭a‬‭scaling‬‭factor‬‭of‬‭1/40‬‭where‬‭both‬‭ProtT5-XL-U50‬‭and‬‭ESM-2‬‭previously‬‭failed‬‭for‬‭the‬‭1X‬
‭architecture.‬‭In‬‭figure‬‭4.13-14‬‭and‬‭B.27-30,‬‭the‬‭validation‬‭performance‬‭of‬‭these‬‭2X‬‭models‬
‭are‬‭compared‬‭to‬‭their‬‭1X‬‭counterparts.‬‭Again,‬‭we‬‭generally‬‭see‬‭an‬‭increase‬‭in‬‭performance‬
‭across‬‭performance‬‭measures‬‭and‬‭scaling‬‭factors‬‭compared‬‭to‬‭the‬‭1X‬‭models.‬‭For‬‭neither‬
‭the‬‭ProtT5-XL-U50‬‭nor‬‭the‬‭ESM-2‬‭embedding‬‭is‬‭it‬‭possible‬‭to‬‭say‬‭at‬‭what‬‭scaling‬‭factor‬‭the‬
‭highest performance is achieved, since none of the scaling factors stand out.‬
‭Fig.‬‭4.12.‬‭Effect‬‭of‬‭learning‬‭rate‬‭on‬‭validation‬‭performance‬‭of‬‭the‬‭2X‬‭ESM-1b‬‭model‬‭measured‬‭by‬‭AUC‬‭0.1.‬
‭A‬‭2X‬‭ESM-1b‬‭model‬‭was‬‭tested‬‭with‬‭half‬‭the‬‭learning‬‭rate‬‭(0.0005)‬‭of‬‭the‬‭original‬‭(0.001)‬‭and‬‭it‬‭was‬‭compared‬‭to‬
‭the‬ ‭2X‬ ‭and‬ ‭1X‬ ‭model‬ ‭with‬ ‭original‬ ‭learning‬ ‭rate.‬ ‭All‬ ‭three‬ ‭models‬ ‭use‬ ‭the‬ ‭sigmoid‬ ‭activation‬ ‭function‬ ‭on‬ ‭the‬
‭convolutional‬‭layer‬‭for‬‭CDRs.‬‭They‬‭are‬‭shown‬‭in‬‭different‬‭colors‬‭on‬‭the‬‭plot.‬‭Different‬‭tested‬‭scaling‬‭factors‬‭are‬
‭shown‬‭along‬‭the‬‭first‬‭axis.‬‭Boxplots‬‭summarize‬‭the‬‭distribution‬‭of‬‭the‬‭performance‬‭of‬‭20‬‭cross-validation‬‭models.‬

‭from‬ ‭the‬ ‭hinge.‬

‭4.7 Compare Final Models‬
‭In‬ ‭the‬ ‭previous‬ ‭section‬ ‭it‬ ‭was‬ ‭shown‬ ‭that‬ ‭the‬ ‭2X‬ ‭models‬ ‭with‬ ‭half‬ ‭learning‬ ‭rate‬ ‭and‬‭the‬
‭sigmoid‬‭activation‬‭function‬‭performed‬‭the‬‭best‬‭for‬‭the‬‭ESM-1b,‬‭ProtT5-XL-U50‬‭and‬‭ESM-2‬
‭embeddings.‬‭They‬‭were‬‭now‬‭compared‬‭to‬‭each‬‭other‬‭and‬‭to‬‭the‬‭BLOSUM50‬‭model‬‭with‬‭the‬
‭ReLU‬ ‭activation‬ ‭function.‬ ‭For‬ ‭all‬ ‭four‬ ‭models,‬ ‭a‬ ‭scaling‬ ‭factor‬ ‭of‬ ‭1/5‬ ‭was‬ ‭chosen.‬ ‭The‬
‭difference in performance between the embeddings was plotted (fig. 4.15, B.31-32).‬
‭There‬ ‭was‬ ‭now‬ ‭observed‬ ‭an‬ ‭even‬ ‭larger‬ ‭gain‬ ‭in‬ ‭performance‬ ‭compared‬ ‭to‬ ‭the‬ ‭base‬
‭BLOSUM50‬ ‭model‬ ‭than‬ ‭what‬ ‭was‬ ‭seen‬ ‭in‬ ‭fig.‬ ‭4.8‬ ‭and‬ ‭B.17-18.‬ ‭By‬‭statistical‬‭hypothesis‬
‭testing‬ ‭it‬ ‭was‬ ‭found‬ ‭that‬ ‭all‬ ‭three‬ ‭models‬ ‭using‬ ‭embeddings‬ ‭produced‬ ‭by‬ ‭transformers‬
‭outperformed‬ ‭the‬ ‭BLOSUM50‬ ‭model‬ ‭significantly,‬ ‭across‬ ‭all‬ ‭three‬ ‭metrics.‬ ‭The‬ ‭ESM-1b‬
‭model‬ ‭had‬ ‭p-values‬ ‭of‬
‭for‬ ‭AUC‬ ‭and‬
‭for‬ ‭both‬‭AUC‬‭0.1‬‭and‬‭PPV.‬‭The‬
‭p-values‬‭for‬‭the‬‭ESM-2‬‭model‬‭were‬
‭for‬‭PPV‬‭and‬
‭for‬‭AUC‬‭and‬‭AUC‬‭0.1.‬
‭Finally,‬‭the‬‭p-values‬‭for‬‭the‬‭ProtT5-XL-U50‬‭model‬‭were‬‭determined‬‭to‬
‭for‬‭PPV‬‭and‬
‭for AUC 0.1 and AUC.‬
‭From‬ ‭the‬ ‭plots‬ ‭the‬ ‭ESM-1b‬ ‭embedding‬ ‭appeared‬ ‭to‬ ‭perform‬ ‭the‬ ‭best.‬ ‭It‬‭had‬‭the‬‭highest‬
‭mean‬‭and‬‭weighted‬‭mean‬‭performance‬‭across‬‭all‬‭performance‬‭metrics‬‭except‬‭its‬‭weighted‬
‭50‬
==PAGE:55==
‭AUC‬‭was‬‭a‬‭little‬‭lower‬‭than‬‭for‬‭the‬‭ProtT5-XL-U50‬‭and‬‭ESM-2‬‭models,‬‭and‬‭its‬‭weighted‬‭AUC‬
‭0.1‬‭was‬‭also‬‭a‬‭little‬‭lower‬‭than‬‭for‬‭the‬‭ESM-2‬‭model.‬‭Especially‬‭the‬‭mean‬‭PPV‬‭was‬‭higher‬‭for‬
‭the‬‭ESM-1b‬‭model‬‭than‬‭for‬‭the‬‭other‬‭two‬‭embeddings.‬‭The‬‭mean‬‭PPV‬‭of‬‭the‬‭ESM-1b‬‭model‬
‭was‬‭about‬‭1.6‬‭percentage‬‭points‬‭larger‬‭than‬‭for‬‭the‬‭ESM-2‬‭model‬‭and‬‭about‬‭1.8‬‭percentage‬
‭points‬ ‭larger‬ ‭than‬ ‭for‬ ‭the‬ ‭ProtT5-XL-U50‬ ‭model.‬ ‭The‬ ‭relatively‬ ‭high‬ ‭mean‬ ‭PPV‬ ‭of‬ ‭the‬
‭ESM-1b‬‭model‬‭compared‬‭to‬‭the‬‭other‬‭two‬‭models‬‭was‬‭due‬‭to‬‭the‬‭relatively‬‭high‬‭PPV‬‭for‬‭a‬
‭couple‬‭of‬‭the‬‭least‬‭abundant‬‭peptides,‬‭namely‬‭RFPLTFGWCF,‬‭CTELKLSDY,‬‭GPRLGVRAT,‬
‭RPPIFIRRL‬ ‭and‬‭FEDLRVLSF.‬‭The‬‭higher‬‭mean‬‭AUC‬‭0.1‬‭of‬‭the‬‭ESM1-b‬‭model‬‭could‬‭like‬
‭PPV‬ ‭be‬ ‭attributed‬ ‭to‬ ‭a‬ ‭couple‬ ‭of‬ ‭the‬ ‭least‬ ‭abundant‬ ‭peptides,‬ ‭namely‬ ‭RFPLTFGWCF,‬
‭CTELKLSDY,‬‭SLFNTVATLY‬‭and‬‭FEDLRVLSF.‬‭For‬‭AUC‬‭only‬‭one‬‭peptide‬‭really‬‭stood‬‭out‬‭for‬
‭the ESM-1b model and that was the least abundant peptide FEDLRVLSF.‬
‭The‬ ‭ESM-2‬ ‭model‬ ‭seemed‬ ‭to‬ ‭be‬ ‭the‬ ‭second‬ ‭best.‬ ‭It‬ ‭was‬ ‭performing‬ ‭better‬ ‭than‬ ‭the‬
‭ProtT5-XL-U50‬ ‭model‬ ‭across‬ ‭all‬ ‭mean‬ ‭and‬ ‭weighted‬ ‭mean‬ ‭performance‬ ‭metrics‬ ‭except‬
‭weighted AUC.‬
‭Statistical‬ ‭hypothesis‬ ‭testing‬ ‭did‬ ‭however‬ ‭not‬ ‭find‬ ‭a‬ ‭significant‬ ‭difference‬ ‭between‬ ‭the‬
‭performance‬‭of‬‭the‬‭three‬‭models‬‭across‬‭the‬‭three‬‭metrics.‬‭The‬‭only‬‭exception‬‭being‬‭that‬‭the‬
‭ESM-1b‬ ‭model‬‭was‬‭found‬‭to‬‭perform‬‭significantly‬‭better‬‭than‬‭the‬‭ProtT5-XL-U50‬‭model‬‭in‬
‭terms of AUC (‬
‭).‬
‭However,‬ ‭the‬ ‭statistical‬ ‭hypothesis‬ ‭testing‬ ‭that‬ ‭was‬ ‭done‬ ‭only‬ ‭looked‬ ‭at‬ ‭the‬ ‭fraction‬ ‭of‬
‭peptides‬‭where‬‭one‬‭model‬‭did‬‭better‬‭than‬‭another‬‭model‬‭in‬‭terms‬‭of‬‭a‬‭performance‬‭metric.‬
‭So‬‭it‬‭would‬‭deem‬‭the‬‭performance‬‭of‬‭two‬‭models‬‭not‬‭significantly‬‭different,‬‭if‬‭the‬‭amount‬‭of‬
‭peptides‬‭where‬‭one‬‭model‬‭did‬‭better‬‭than‬‭the‬‭other‬‭was‬‭about‬‭the‬‭same‬‭for‬‭the‬‭two‬‭models,‬
‭even‬ ‭though‬ ‭that‬ ‭for‬ ‭one‬ ‭of‬ ‭the‬ ‭models‬ ‭the‬ ‭half‬ ‭of‬ ‭peptides‬ ‭where‬ ‭it‬ ‭did‬ ‭have‬ ‭a‬ ‭higher‬
‭performance‬ ‭than‬ ‭the‬ ‭other‬ ‭model‬ ‭there‬ ‭was‬ ‭a‬ ‭good‬ ‭portion‬ ‭that‬ ‭had‬ ‭a‬ ‭quite‬ ‭large‬
‭performance‬‭compared‬‭to‬‭the‬‭other‬‭model‬‭and‬‭for‬‭the‬‭half‬‭where‬‭it‬‭did‬‭worse‬‭it‬‭was‬‭generally‬
‭only‬‭doing‬‭a‬‭little‬‭worse‬‭than‬‭the‬‭other‬‭model.‬‭This‬‭seemed‬‭to‬‭be‬‭the‬‭case‬‭for‬‭the‬‭ESM-1b‬
‭model‬‭when‬‭it‬‭was‬‭compared‬‭to‬‭the‬‭other‬‭two‬‭models‬‭in‬‭terms‬‭of‬‭AUC‬‭0.1‬‭and‬‭PPV‬‭(fig.‬‭4.15‬
‭and B.32).‬
‭Taking‬‭this‬‭into‬‭consideration‬‭the‬‭ESM-1b‬‭model‬‭was‬‭in‬‭the‬‭end‬‭deemed‬‭the‬‭better‬‭model‬‭of‬
‭the‬ ‭three,‬ ‭if‬ ‭only‬ ‭marginally.‬ ‭It‬ ‭was‬ ‭found‬ ‭to‬ ‭perform‬ ‭significantly‬ ‭better‬ ‭than‬ ‭the‬
‭ProtT5-XL-U50‬‭model‬‭in‬‭terms‬‭of‬‭AUC,‬‭it‬‭was‬‭found‬‭to‬‭have‬‭the‬‭highest‬‭mean‬‭performance‬
‭of‬ ‭the‬ ‭three‬ ‭models‬ ‭for‬ ‭all‬ ‭metrics,‬ ‭it‬ ‭was‬ ‭found‬ ‭to‬ ‭have‬ ‭comparable‬ ‭weighted‬ ‭mean‬
‭performance‬‭to‬‭the‬‭other‬‭two‬‭models‬‭in‬‭terms‬‭of‬‭all‬‭three‬‭metrics‬‭and‬‭it‬‭was‬‭found‬‭to‬‭have‬‭a‬
‭relatively‬‭high‬‭PPV‬‭and‬‭AUC‬‭0.1‬‭for‬‭a‬‭couple‬‭of‬‭the‬‭least‬‭abundant‬‭peptides‬‭compared‬‭to‬‭the‬
‭other two models.‬
‭51‬
==PAGE:56==
‭Fig.‬ ‭4.15.‬‭Difference‬‭in‬‭test‬‭performance‬‭between‬‭final‬‭version‬‭of‬‭models‬‭with‬‭new‬‭embeddings‬‭and‬‭the‬
‭baseline‬ ‭model‬ ‭measured‬ ‭by‬ ‭ΔAUC‬ ‭0.1.‬‭In‬‭the‬‭final‬‭version‬‭of‬‭models‬‭with‬‭new‬‭embeddings‬‭an‬‭architecture‬
‭size‬‭of‬‭2X‬‭is‬‭used‬‭with‬‭a‬‭scaling‬‭factor‬‭of‬‭1/5,‬‭a‬‭learning‬‭rate‬‭of‬‭0.0005‬‭and‬‭the‬‭sigmoid‬‭activation‬‭function‬‭applied‬
‭to‬‭the‬‭convolutional‬‭layer‬‭for‬‭CDRs.‬‭The‬‭embeddings‬‭of‬‭the‬‭final‬‭models‬‭are‬‭ESM-1b,‬‭ProtT5-XL-U50‬‭and‬‭ESM-2‬
‭indicated‬‭by‬‭different‬‭colors.‬‭The‬‭performance‬‭of‬‭the‬‭baseline‬‭BLOSUM50-embedded‬‭model‬‭is‬‭used‬‭as‬‭the‬‭origin‬
‭and‬ ‭the‬ ‭performance‬ ‭of‬ ‭the‬ ‭other‬ ‭three‬ ‭models‬ ‭are‬ ‭given‬ ‭as‬ ‭ΔAUC‬‭0.1‬‭relative‬‭to‬‭this‬‭origin.‬‭The‬‭per‬‭peptide‬
‭difference‬‭in‬‭performance‬‭is‬‭shown‬‭to‬‭the‬‭right,‬‭where‬‭peptides‬‭are‬‭sorted‬‭from‬‭the‬‭most‬‭abundant‬‭peptide‬‭to‬‭the‬
‭least‬‭abundant‬‭peptide‬‭only‬‭counting‬‭positive‬‭peptides.‬‭The‬‭difference‬‭in‬‭mean‬‭and‬‭weighted‬‭mean‬‭performance‬
‭taken‬ ‭over‬ ‭all‬ ‭peptides‬‭is‬‭shown‬‭to‬‭the‬‭left,‬‭where‬‭the‬‭weighted‬‭mean‬‭performance‬‭weights‬‭peptides‬‭after‬‭their‬
‭occurrence.‬‭Numbers‬‭in‬‭parentheses‬‭in‬‭labels‬‭along‬‭the‬‭first‬‭axis‬‭are‬‭the‬‭occurrence‬‭of‬‭positive‬‭peptides‬‭in‬‭each‬
‭group.‬
‭52‬
==PAGE:57==
‭5 Discussion‬
‭This‬ ‭study‬ ‭explored‬ ‭whether‬ ‭incorporating‬ ‭language‬ ‭models‬ ‭in‬ ‭the‬ ‭form‬ ‭of‬ ‭transformers,‬
‭specifically‬ ‭ESM-1b,‬ ‭ProtT5-XL-U50,‬ ‭and‬ ‭ESM-2,‬ ‭for‬ ‭embedding‬ ‭input‬ ‭sequences‬ ‭would‬
‭improve‬ ‭the‬ ‭predictive‬ ‭capability‬ ‭of‬ ‭neural‬ ‭networks‬ ‭for‬ ‭TCR‬ ‭specificity,‬ ‭as‬ ‭opposed‬ ‭to‬
‭utilizing‬ ‭a‬ ‭more‬ ‭conventional‬ ‭BLOSUM-based‬ ‭encoding.‬ ‭These‬ ‭transformers‬ ‭were‬
‭pre-trained‬ ‭on‬ ‭extensive‬ ‭protein‬ ‭sequence‬ ‭datasets‬ ‭to‬ ‭grasp‬ ‭general‬ ‭patterns‬ ‭in‬ ‭protein‬
‭sequences.‬ ‭The‬ ‭utilized‬ ‭neural‬ ‭networks‬ ‭were‬ ‭variations‬ ‭of‬ ‭the‬ ‭NetTCR‬ ‭CNN‬ ‭with‬ ‭a‬
‭max-pooled architecture.‬
‭Results‬ ‭indicated‬ ‭that‬ ‭for‬ ‭all‬ ‭three‬ ‭transformers,‬ ‭the‬ ‭embedded‬ ‭input‬ ‭sequences‬ ‭yielded‬
‭improved‬ ‭TCR‬ ‭specificity‬ ‭predictions‬ ‭compared‬ ‭to‬ ‭BLOSUM-encoded‬ ‭input‬ ‭sequences.‬
‭Among‬ ‭the‬ ‭transformers,‬ ‭ESM-1b‬ ‭exhibited‬ ‭the‬ ‭highest‬ ‭model‬ ‭performance,‬ ‭albeit‬ ‭only‬
‭marginally surpassing the other two.‬
‭Furthermore,‬‭the‬‭study‬‭identified‬‭that‬‭proper‬‭scaling‬‭of‬‭the‬‭input‬‭space,‬‭the‬‭selection‬‭of‬‭the‬
‭network‬‭activation‬‭function,‬‭and‬‭adjustments‬‭to‬‭the‬‭dimensions‬‭of‬‭the‬‭neural‬‭network‬‭were‬‭all‬
‭factors influencing predictive power.‬
‭All‬‭models‬‭in‬‭the‬‭project‬‭were‬‭trained‬‭with‬‭early‬‭stopping‬‭with‬‭a‬‭patience‬‭of‬‭100‬‭epochs‬‭and‬
‭validation‬‭AUC‬‭0.1‬‭as‬‭a‬‭stopping‬‭criterion.‬‭In‬‭retrospect‬‭when‬‭looking‬‭at‬‭the‬‭learning‬‭curves‬‭it‬
‭seems‬‭like‬‭that‬‭this‬‭setup‬‭resulted‬‭in‬‭that‬‭training‬‭was‬‭generally‬‭stopped‬‭too‬‭late.‬‭Meaning‬
‭that‬‭when‬‭training‬‭was‬‭stopped,‬‭validation‬‭loss‬‭had‬‭already‬‭passed‬‭its‬‭minimum‬‭value‬‭many‬
‭epochs‬‭ago‬‭and‬‭increased‬‭by‬‭quite‬‭a‬‭lot‬‭while‬‭validation‬‭AUC‬‭0.1‬‭for‬‭many‬‭epochs‬‭had‬‭only‬
‭increased‬‭by‬‭a‬‭very‬‭small‬‭amount‬‭(see‬‭fig.‬‭C.13‬‭and‬‭C.15).‬‭This‬‭means‬‭that‬‭the‬‭models‬‭were‬
‭generally‬‭overfitted‬‭with‬‭respect‬‭to‬‭loss‬‭and‬‭that‬‭training‬‭time‬‭was‬‭much‬‭longer‬‭than‬‭needed.‬
‭A‬‭better‬‭setup‬‭could‬‭therefore‬‭likely‬‭have‬‭been‬‭to‬‭use‬‭a‬‭weighted‬‭average‬‭of‬‭validation‬‭AUC‬
‭0.1‬‭and‬‭the‬‭reciprocal‬‭of‬‭the‬‭validation‬‭loss‬‭as‬‭stopping‬‭criterion.‬‭This‬‭way‬‭loss‬‭also‬‭has‬‭an‬
‭influence‬‭on‬‭when‬‭to‬‭stop‬‭training.‬‭Since‬‭a‬‭lower‬‭validation‬‭loss‬‭but‬‭a‬‭higher‬‭validation‬‭AUC‬
‭0.1‬‭is‬‭better,‬‭the‬‭reciprocal‬‭of‬‭the‬‭validation‬‭loss‬‭should‬‭be‬‭used‬‭in‬‭the‬‭weighted‬‭average.‬
‭Another‬ ‭and‬ ‭maybe‬ ‭even‬ ‭better‬ ‭solution‬ ‭would‬ ‭be‬ ‭to‬ ‭still‬ ‭use‬ ‭validation‬ ‭AUC‬ ‭0.1‬ ‭as‬ ‭a‬
‭stopping‬ ‭criterion‬ ‭but‬ ‭to‬ ‭use‬ ‭the‬ ‭“min_delta”‬ ‭parameter‬ ‭in‬ ‭Keras.‬ ‭With‬ ‭this‬ ‭parameter‬ ‭a‬
‭minimum‬‭change‬‭in‬‭validation‬‭AUC‬‭0.1‬‭to‬‭qualify‬‭as‬‭an‬‭improvement‬‭can‬‭be‬‭specified.‬‭This‬
‭means‬‭that‬‭if‬‭the‬‭increase‬‭in‬‭validation‬‭AUC‬‭0.1‬‭over‬‭100‬‭epochs‬‭is‬‭deemed‬‭too‬‭small‬‭to‬‭be‬
‭considered an improvement, the training process will be halted.‬
‭When‬‭increasing‬‭the‬‭model‬‭architecture‬‭from‬‭1X‬‭to‬‭2X‬‭for‬‭the‬‭ESM-1b‬‭model,‬‭it‬‭was‬‭found‬
‭that‬‭the‬‭range‬‭of‬‭scaling‬‭factors,‬‭within‬‭which‬‭models‬‭initiated‬‭learning,‬‭greatly‬‭narrowed‬‭for‬
‭the‬ ‭sigmoid‬ ‭function.‬ ‭In‬ ‭contrast‬ ‭the‬ ‭2X‬ ‭ReLU‬ ‭models‬ ‭demonstrated‬ ‭learning‬ ‭across‬ ‭the‬
‭same‬ ‭scaling‬ ‭factors‬ ‭as‬ ‭their‬ ‭1X‬ ‭counterparts‬ ‭(that‬ ‭is‬ ‭for‬ ‭those‬ ‭scaling‬‭factors‬‭that‬‭were‬
‭actually‬‭tested‬‭for‬‭the‬‭2X‬‭architecture).‬‭However,‬‭the‬‭window‬‭of‬‭scaling‬‭factors‬‭where‬‭models‬
‭performed‬ ‭the‬ ‭best‬ ‭became‬ ‭narrower‬ ‭for‬ ‭the‬ ‭ReLU‬ ‭function,‬ ‭when‬ ‭going‬ ‭from‬ ‭the‬ ‭1X‬
‭architecture‬‭to‬‭the‬‭2X‬‭architecture.‬‭When‬‭halving‬‭the‬‭learning‬‭rate‬‭for‬‭2X‬‭ESM-1b‬‭sigmoid‬
‭models,‬ ‭it‬ ‭was‬ ‭found‬ ‭that‬ ‭the‬ ‭model‬ ‭performance‬ ‭increased‬ ‭and‬ ‭that‬ ‭all‬ ‭cross-validation‬
‭models‬ ‭for‬ ‭all‬ ‭tested‬ ‭scaling‬ ‭factors‬ ‭started‬ ‭learning,‬ ‭where‬ ‭the‬ ‭2X‬ ‭models‬ ‭with‬ ‭original‬
‭learning‬‭rate‬‭failed.‬‭When‬‭comparing‬‭the‬‭learning‬‭curves‬‭for‬‭the‬‭2X‬‭ESM-1b‬‭sigmoid‬‭models‬
‭with‬ ‭original‬ ‭and‬‭half‬‭learning‬‭rate,‬‭it‬‭is‬‭noticed‬‭that‬‭models‬‭with‬‭the‬‭original‬‭learning‬‭rate‬
‭53‬
==PAGE:58==
‭experienced‬‭a‬‭plateau‬‭at‬‭the‬‭beginning‬‭of‬‭learning‬‭for‬‭many‬‭of‬‭the‬‭cross-validation‬‭models‬
‭for‬‭most‬‭of‬‭the‬‭tested‬‭scaling‬‭factors.‬‭For‬‭many‬‭scaling‬‭factors‬‭some‬‭of‬‭the‬‭cross-validation‬
‭models‬‭seemed‬‭to‬‭be‬‭stuck‬‭in‬‭this‬‭plateau‬‭and‬‭never‬‭started‬‭learning,‬‭causing‬‭the‬‭model‬‭to‬
‭fail.‬ ‭The‬ ‭plateaus‬ ‭were‬ ‭mostly‬ ‭gone‬ ‭for‬ ‭models‬ ‭with‬ ‭half‬ ‭the‬ ‭learning‬ ‭rate,‬ ‭being‬ ‭only‬
‭observed‬ ‭to‬ ‭a‬ ‭small‬ ‭degree‬ ‭for‬ ‭the‬ ‭smallest‬ ‭of‬ ‭the‬ ‭tested‬ ‭learning‬ ‭factors.‬ ‭This‬ ‭is‬ ‭both‬
‭surprising‬ ‭and‬ ‭seems‬ ‭counterintuitive.‬ ‭Normally‬ ‭a‬‭higher‬‭learning‬‭rate,‬‭not‬‭a‬‭smaller‬‭one,‬
‭would‬‭help‬‭a‬‭model‬‭to‬‭get‬‭unstuck‬‭from‬‭a‬‭plateau.‬‭An‬‭explanation‬‭might‬‭be‬‭that‬‭the‬‭higher‬
‭learning‬ ‭rate‬ ‭causes‬ ‭the‬ ‭stochastic‬ ‭gradient‬ ‭descent‬ ‭process‬ ‭to‬ ‭diverge‬ ‭away‬ ‭from‬ ‭the‬
‭optimum‬‭right‬‭from‬‭the‬‭beginning‬‭of‬‭learning‬‭into‬‭a‬‭region‬‭of‬‭the‬‭error‬‭landscape‬‭that‬‭is‬‭flat.‬‭It‬
‭then has trouble finding back to the optimum.‬
‭In‬‭addition‬‭to‬‭a‬‭too‬‭high‬‭learning‬‭rate,‬‭the‬‭plateau‬‭at‬‭the‬‭beginning‬‭of‬‭learning‬‭also‬‭appears‬‭to‬
‭be‬‭caused‬‭by‬‭a‬‭high‬‭model‬‭complexity‬‭and‬‭the‬‭use‬‭of‬‭the‬‭sigmoid‬‭function,‬‭since‬‭1X‬‭sigmoid‬
‭models‬ ‭did‬ ‭not‬ ‭experience‬ ‭plataus‬ ‭at‬ ‭the‬ ‭beginning‬ ‭for‬ ‭nearly‬ ‭as‬ ‭many‬ ‭different‬ ‭scaling‬
‭factors,‬‭and‬‭almost‬‭no‬‭ReLU‬‭models‬‭had‬‭a‬‭plateau.‬‭The‬‭only‬‭ReLU‬‭models‬‭with‬‭plateaus‬
‭were‬‭those‬‭that‬‭had‬‭a‬‭scaling‬‭factor‬‭of‬‭1‬‭and‬‭the‬‭1X‬‭ESM-1b‬‭with‬‭a‬‭scaling‬‭factor‬‭of‬‭1/5.‬‭That‬
‭models‬ ‭that‬ ‭employ‬ ‭the‬ ‭sigmoid‬ ‭function‬ ‭are‬ ‭more‬ ‭susceptible‬ ‭to‬ ‭plataus‬ ‭compared‬ ‭to‬
‭models‬‭that‬‭use‬‭the‬‭ReLU‬‭function‬‭is‬‭not‬‭surprising,‬‭since‬‭neurons‬‭activated‬‭by‬‭the‬‭sigmoid‬
‭function‬‭are‬‭easier‬‭to‬‭saturate.‬‭The‬‭derivative‬‭of‬‭the‬‭sigmoid‬‭function‬‭has‬‭a‬‭relatively‬‭small‬
‭interval‬‭where‬‭it‬‭is‬‭sufficiently‬‭nonzero‬‭compared‬‭to‬‭the‬‭derivative‬‭of‬‭the‬‭ReLU‬‭function‬‭(see‬
‭fig.‬‭2.2).‬‭Put‬‭differently,‬‭when‬‭a‬‭sigmoid‬‭function‬‭approaches‬‭either‬‭the‬‭left‬‭or‬‭right‬‭plateau,‬
‭performing‬‭a‬‭backward‬‭pass‬‭through‬‭it‬‭becomes‬‭almost‬‭irrelevant,‬‭as‬‭the‬‭derivative‬‭becomes‬
‭very close to zero‬‭(Thakur 2023)‬‭.‬
‭A‬‭final‬‭cause‬‭for‬‭the‬‭plataus‬‭was‬‭the‬‭scaling‬‭factor.‬‭In‬‭all‬‭cases‬‭for‬‭models‬‭using‬‭the‬‭sigmoid‬
‭function,‬‭it‬‭was‬‭observed‬‭that‬‭small‬‭scaling‬‭factors‬‭resulted‬‭in‬‭plateaus‬‭in‬‭the‬‭beginning‬‭of‬
‭learning‬‭and‬‭that‬‭the‬‭plateaus‬‭became‬‭worse‬‭as‬‭the‬‭scaling‬‭factor‬‭was‬‭reduced,‬‭eventually‬
‭resulting‬‭in‬‭that‬‭multiple‬‭of‬‭cross-validation‬‭models‬‭did‬‭not‬‭start‬‭learning.‬‭It‬‭was‬‭however‬‭in‬
‭one‬ ‭case‬ ‭also‬ ‭observed‬ ‭that‬ ‭a‬ ‭too‬ ‭large‬ ‭scaling‬ ‭factor‬ ‭resulted‬ ‭in‬ ‭multiple‬ ‭of‬ ‭the‬
‭cross-validation‬ ‭models‬ ‭to‬ ‭not‬ ‭start‬ ‭learning‬ ‭and‬ ‭that‬‭was‬‭for‬‭the‬‭2X‬‭ESM-1b‬‭model‬‭with‬
‭original‬‭learning‬‭rate‬‭and‬‭a‬‭scaling‬‭factor‬‭of‬‭1.‬‭The‬‭reason‬‭why‬‭too‬‭small‬‭or‬‭too‬‭large‬‭scaling‬
‭factors‬ ‭resulted‬ ‭in‬ ‭plateaus‬ ‭or‬‭no‬‭learning‬‭is‬‭not‬‭yet‬‭understood.‬‭It‬‭might‬‭have‬‭to‬‭do‬‭with‬
‭"contours"‬‭of‬‭the‬‭optimization‬‭landscape‬‭becoming‬‭narrow‬‭for‬‭large‬‭or‬‭small‬‭scaling‬‭factors‬
‭causing the stochastic gradient process having a harder time finding the optimum.‬
‭It‬‭was‬‭found‬‭that‬‭certain‬‭scaling‬‭factors‬‭lead‬‭to‬‭better‬‭model‬‭performance‬‭than‬‭others‬‭and‬
‭that‬‭some‬‭scaling‬‭factors‬‭resulted‬‭in‬‭that‬‭multiple‬‭of‬‭the‬‭cross-validation‬‭models‬‭did‬‭not‬‭start‬
‭learning.‬‭It‬‭was‬‭seen‬‭for‬‭the‬‭ESM-1b‬‭that‬‭when‬‭the‬‭architecture‬‭size‬‭is‬‭doubled‬‭from‬‭1X‬‭to‬
‭2X‬‭the‬‭dependence‬‭on‬‭proper‬‭scaling‬‭increases.‬‭However,‬‭when‬‭the‬‭learning‬‭rate‬‭is‬‭halved‬
‭for‬‭the‬‭2X‬‭sigmoid‬‭models‬‭this‬‭dependence‬‭seems‬‭to‬‭almost‬‭disappear.‬‭It‬‭is‬‭possible‬‭that‬
‭halving‬‭the‬‭learning‬‭rate‬‭for‬‭the‬‭1X‬‭models‬‭and‬‭the‬‭ReLU‬‭models‬‭will‬‭reduce‬‭the‬‭dependence‬
‭on‬‭the‬‭scaling‬‭factor‬‭as‬‭well.‬‭If‬‭that‬‭is‬‭the‬‭case‬‭it‬‭would‬‭greatly‬‭ease‬‭model‬‭development,‬
‭since‬‭different‬‭scaling‬‭factors‬‭would‬‭not‬‭have‬‭to‬‭be‬‭tested.‬‭What‬‭causes‬‭some‬‭scaling‬‭factors‬
‭to give better model performance is not understood.‬
‭CNN‬ ‭models,‬ ‭utilizing‬ ‭embeddings‬ ‭generated‬ ‭from‬ ‭one‬ ‭of‬ ‭the‬ ‭three‬ ‭transformers,‬
‭demonstrated‬ ‭notably‬ ‭improved‬ ‭performance‬ ‭when‬ ‭the‬ ‭convolutional‬ ‭layers‬‭for‬‭the‬‭CDRs‬
‭were‬‭activated‬‭by‬‭the‬‭sigmoid‬‭activation‬‭function‬‭as‬‭opposed‬‭to‬‭the‬‭ReLU‬‭activation‬‭function.‬
‭54‬
==PAGE:59==
‭This‬‭is‬‭rather‬‭surprising‬‭since‬‭the‬‭ReLU‬‭function‬‭is‬‭generally‬‭recommended‬‭over‬‭the‬‭sigmoid‬
‭function‬‭and‬‭in‬‭a‬‭recent‬‭benchmark‬‭(Dubey,‬‭Singh,‬‭and‬‭Chaudhuri‬‭2021)‬‭the‬‭ReLU‬‭function‬
‭was‬ ‭found‬ ‭to‬ ‭lead‬ ‭to‬‭better‬‭model‬‭performance‬‭than‬‭the‬‭sigmoid‬‭function‬‭across‬‭different‬
‭kinds of CNNs.‬
‭A‬ ‭potential‬ ‭explanation‬‭for‬‭the‬‭worse‬‭performance‬‭when‬‭utilizing‬‭the‬‭ReLU‬‭function‬‭is‬‭the‬
‭“dying‬‭ReLU”‬‭problem,‬‭where‬‭some‬‭neurons‬‭of‬‭the‬‭network‬‭effectively‬‭“die”,‬‭meaning‬‭they‬
‭stop‬‭outputting‬‭anything‬‭other‬‭than‬‭zero‬‭(Géron‬‭2019)‬‭.‬‭If‬‭too‬‭many‬‭neurons‬‭are‬‭dead‬‭it‬‭will‬
‭hinder the network's ability to probably learn the patterns of the input.‬
‭One‬ ‭cause‬ ‭for‬ ‭the‬‭dying‬‭ReLU‬‭problem‬‭is‬‭a‬‭too‬‭high‬‭learning‬‭rate.‬‭Since‬‭the‬‭2X‬‭sigmoid‬
‭models‬‭benefited‬‭from‬‭reducing‬‭the‬‭learning‬‭rate‬‭it‬‭is‬‭suspected‬‭that‬‭the‬‭learning‬‭rate‬‭was‬
‭also set too high for the ReLU function.‬
‭Another‬‭cause‬‭is‬‭the‬‭use‬‭of‬‭an‬‭inappropriate‬‭weight‬‭initializer‬‭for‬‭initializing‬‭the‬‭weights‬‭of‬
‭neurons‬ ‭activated‬ ‭by‬ ‭ReLU.‬ ‭All‬ ‭weights‬ ‭were‬ ‭initialized‬ ‭by‬ ‭the‬ ‭Glorot‬ ‭uniform‬ ‭initializer.‬
‭However,‬‭this‬‭initializer‬‭is‬‭designed‬‭for‬‭weights‬‭of‬‭neurons‬‭activated‬‭by‬‭sigmoid.‬‭A‬‭different‬
‭initializer,‬‭known‬‭as‬‭the‬‭He‬‭initializer‬‭(He‬‭et‬‭al.‬‭2015)‬‭(existing‬‭in‬‭both‬‭an‬‭uniform‬‭and‬‭normal‬
‭version) is designed for the ReLU function and should be tested.‬
‭To‬ ‭investigate‬ ‭if‬ ‭ReLU‬ ‭models‬ ‭suffer‬ ‭from‬ ‭the‬ ‭“dying‬ ‭ReLU”‬ ‭problem,‬ ‭the‬ ‭outputs‬ ‭and‬
‭gradients of ReLU activated neurons can be plotted.‬
‭When‬ ‭testing‬ ‭the‬ ‭different‬ ‭transformers‬ ‭only‬ ‭the‬ ‭CDR‬ ‭sequences‬ ‭were‬ ‭embedded.‬ ‭The‬
‭peptide‬‭sequences‬‭were‬‭in‬‭all‬‭cases‬‭encoded‬‭by‬‭BLOSUM50,‬‭the‬‭reason‬‭being‬‭that‬‭all‬‭the‬
‭tested‬‭transformers‬‭are‬‭intended‬‭to‬‭be‬‭used‬‭on‬‭full‬‭protein‬‭sequences.‬‭This‬‭means‬‭that‬‭they‬
‭would‬‭likely‬‭not‬‭give‬‭meaningful‬‭results‬‭if‬‭the‬‭peptide‬‭sequences‬‭were‬‭directly‬‭used‬‭as‬‭input‬
‭to‬‭the‬‭transformers.‬‭One‬‭would‬‭instead‬‭have‬‭to‬‭find‬‭the‬‭full‬‭protein‬‭sequence‬‭that‬‭a‬‭given‬
‭peptide‬ ‭sequence‬ ‭stems‬ ‭from‬ ‭by‬‭e.g.‬‭using‬‭BLAST‬‭(Altschul‬‭et‬‭al.‬‭1990)‬‭and‬‭use‬‭this‬‭as‬
‭input‬ ‭to‬ ‭the‬ ‭transformer.‬ ‭Then‬ ‭the‬ ‭peptide‬ ‭embedding‬ ‭could‬ ‭be‬ ‭cut‬ ‭out‬ ‭of‬ ‭the‬ ‭protein‬
‭embedding.‬‭This‬‭was‬‭however‬‭not‬‭done‬‭in‬‭this‬‭project‬‭due‬‭to‬‭time‬‭limitations,‬‭but‬‭could‬‭be‬
‭interesting to investigate in a future one.‬
‭The‬‭ESM-1b‬‭model‬‭was‬‭in‬‭the‬‭end‬‭deemed‬‭the‬‭better‬‭model‬‭of‬‭the‬‭three‬‭taking‬‭in‬‭sequences‬
‭embedded‬ ‭by‬ ‭transformers.‬ ‭However,‬ ‭one‬ ‭has‬ ‭to‬ ‭remember‬ ‭that‬ ‭other‬ ‭sets‬ ‭of‬
‭hyperparameters‬‭might‬‭result‬‭in‬‭one‬‭of‬‭the‬‭other‬‭models‬‭coming‬‭up‬‭on‬‭top.‬‭For‬‭example‬‭in‬
‭the‬ ‭initial‬ ‭comparison‬ ‭of‬ ‭the‬ ‭three‬ ‭models‬ ‭where‬ ‭hyperparameters‬ ‭were‬ ‭not‬‭adjusted‬‭the‬
‭ESM-1b model clearly did the worst.‬
‭In‬‭conclusion‬‭it‬‭was‬‭found‬‭for‬‭the‬‭tested‬‭neural‬‭networks‬‭that‬‭the‬‭prediction‬‭of‬‭TCR‬‭specificity‬
‭could‬‭significantly‬‭be‬‭improved‬‭by‬‭using‬‭embedded‬‭sequences‬‭for‬‭the‬‭CDRs‬‭as‬‭input‬‭instead‬
‭of‬‭BLOSUM50‬‭encoded‬‭sequences.‬‭To‬‭get‬‭the‬‭best‬‭performance‬‭possible‬‭one‬‭would‬‭have‬‭to‬
‭fine-tune the hyperparameters.‬

‭Appendix B - Figures‬
‭Fig‬‭B.1.‬‭Effect‬‭of‬‭dropout‬‭and‬‭loss‬‭weighting‬‭on‬‭model‬‭test‬‭performance‬‭measured‬‭by‬‭AUC.‬‭Combinations‬
‭of‬‭including/excluding‬‭dropout‬‭and‬‭loss‬‭weighting‬‭results‬‭in‬‭four‬‭tested‬‭models,‬‭each‬‭shown‬‭by‬‭a‬‭different‬‭color.‬
‭The‬‭per‬‭peptide‬‭performance‬‭is‬‭shown‬‭to‬‭the‬‭right,‬‭where‬‭peptides‬‭are‬‭sorted‬‭from‬‭the‬‭most‬‭abundant‬‭peptide‬‭to‬
‭the‬ ‭least‬ ‭abundant‬ ‭peptide‬ ‭only‬ ‭counting‬ ‭positive‬ ‭peptides.‬ ‭The‬ ‭mean‬ ‭and‬‭weighted‬‭mean‬‭performance‬‭taken‬
‭over‬ ‭all‬ ‭peptides‬ ‭is‬ ‭shown‬ ‭to‬ ‭the‬ ‭left,‬ ‭where‬ ‭the‬ ‭weighted‬ ‭mean‬ ‭performance‬ ‭weights‬ ‭peptides‬ ‭after‬ ‭their‬
‭occurrence.‬‭Numbers‬‭in‬‭parentheses‬‭in‬‭labels‬‭along‬‭the‬‭first‬‭axis‬‭are‬‭the‬‭occurrence‬‭of‬‭positive‬‭peptides‬‭in‬‭each‬
‭group.‬

‭Fig‬ ‭B.3.‬ ‭Effect‬ ‭of‬ ‭dropout‬ ‭and‬ ‭loss‬ ‭weighting‬ ‭on‬ ‭model‬ ‭test‬ ‭performance‬ ‭measured‬ ‭by‬ ‭ΔAUC.‬
‭Combinations‬‭of‬‭including/excluding‬‭dropout‬‭and‬‭loss‬‭weighting‬‭results‬‭in‬‭four‬‭tested‬‭models,‬‭where‬‭three‬‭of‬‭them‬
‭are‬‭shown‬‭by‬‭a‬‭different‬‭color.‬‭The‬‭performance‬‭of‬‭the‬‭fourth‬‭model‬‭with‬‭no‬‭dropout‬‭and‬‭no‬‭loss‬‭weighting‬‭is‬‭used‬
‭as‬ ‭the‬ ‭origin‬ ‭and‬ ‭the‬‭performance‬‭of‬‭the‬‭other‬‭three‬‭models‬‭are‬‭given‬‭as‬‭ΔAUC‬‭relative‬‭to‬‭this‬‭origin.‬‭The‬‭per‬
‭peptide‬ ‭difference‬ ‭in‬ ‭performance‬ ‭is‬ ‭shown‬ ‭to‬ ‭the‬ ‭right,‬ ‭where‬ ‭peptides‬ ‭are‬ ‭sorted‬ ‭from‬ ‭the‬ ‭most‬ ‭abundant‬
‭peptide‬‭to‬‭the‬‭least‬‭abundant‬‭peptide‬‭only‬‭counting‬‭positive‬‭peptides.‬‭The‬‭difference‬‭in‬‭mean‬‭and‬‭weighted‬‭mean‬
‭performance‬‭taken‬‭over‬‭all‬‭peptides‬‭is‬‭shown‬‭to‬‭the‬‭left,‬‭where‬‭the‬‭weighted‬‭mean‬‭performance‬‭weights‬‭peptides‬
‭after‬ ‭their‬ ‭occurrence.‬ ‭Numbers‬ ‭in‬ ‭parentheses‬ ‭in‬ ‭labels‬ ‭along‬ ‭the‬ ‭first‬ ‭axis‬ ‭are‬ ‭the‬ ‭occurrence‬ ‭of‬ ‭positive‬
‭peptides in each group.‬

‭of‬‭the‬‭performance‬‭of‬‭20‬‭cross-validation‬‭models.‬‭Whiskers‬‭extend‬‭to‬‭the‬‭largest/smallest‬‭performance‬‭no‬‭further‬
‭than‬‭a‬‭distance‬‭of‬
‭from‬‭the‬‭hinge.‬‭Outliers‬‭are‬‭defined‬‭as‬‭values‬‭with‬‭a‬‭distance‬‭greater‬‭than‬
‭1‬. ‭5‬ · ‭𝐼𝑄𝑅‬
‭1‬. ‭5‬ · ‭𝐼𝑄𝑅‬
‭from‬‭the‬‭hinge‬‭and‬‭are‬‭shown‬‭as‬‭circles.‬‭The‬‭averages‬‭taken‬‭over‬‭the‬‭20‬‭cross-validation‬‭models‬‭are‬‭shown‬‭as‬
‭crosses.‬

==PAGE:81==
‭Fig.‬ ‭B.17.‬ ‭Difference‬ ‭in‬ ‭test‬‭performance‬‭between‬‭second‬‭version‬‭of‬‭models‬‭with‬‭new‬‭embeddings‬‭and‬
‭the‬ ‭baseline‬ ‭model‬ ‭measured‬ ‭by‬ ‭ΔAUC.‬ ‭In‬ ‭the‬ ‭second‬ ‭version‬‭of‬‭models‬‭with‬‭new‬‭embeddings‬‭the‬‭scaling‬
‭factor‬‭has‬‭been‬‭optimized‬‭to‬‭a‬‭value‬‭of‬‭1/20‬‭and‬‭the‬‭sigmoid‬‭activation‬‭function‬‭is‬‭used‬‭on‬‭the‬‭convolutional‬‭layer‬
‭for‬‭CDRs‬‭instead‬‭of‬‭ReLU.‬‭The‬‭embeddings‬‭of‬‭the‬‭models‬‭are‬‭ESM-1b,‬‭ProtT5-XL-U50‬‭and‬‭ESM-2‬‭indicated‬‭by‬
‭different‬ ‭colors.‬ ‭The‬ ‭performance‬ ‭of‬ ‭the‬ ‭baseline‬ ‭BLOSUM50-embedded‬ ‭model‬ ‭is‬ ‭used‬ ‭as‬ ‭the‬ ‭origin‬‭and‬‭the‬
‭performance‬ ‭of‬ ‭the‬ ‭other‬ ‭three‬ ‭models‬ ‭are‬ ‭given‬‭as‬‭ΔAUC‬‭relative‬‭to‬‭this‬‭origin.‬‭The‬‭per‬‭peptide‬‭difference‬‭in‬
‭performance‬ ‭is‬ ‭shown‬ ‭to‬ ‭the‬ ‭right,‬ ‭where‬ ‭peptides‬ ‭are‬ ‭sorted‬ ‭from‬ ‭the‬ ‭most‬ ‭abundant‬ ‭peptide‬ ‭to‬ ‭the‬ ‭least‬
‭abundant‬‭peptide‬‭only‬‭counting‬‭positive‬‭peptides.‬‭The‬‭difference‬‭in‬‭mean‬‭and‬‭weighted‬‭mean‬‭performance‬‭taken‬
‭over‬ ‭all‬ ‭peptides‬ ‭is‬ ‭shown‬ ‭to‬ ‭the‬ ‭left,‬ ‭where‬ ‭the‬ ‭weighted‬ ‭mean‬ ‭performance‬ ‭weights‬ ‭peptides‬ ‭after‬ ‭their‬
‭occurrence.‬‭Numbers‬‭in‬‭parentheses‬‭in‬‭labels‬‭along‬‭the‬‭first‬‭axis‬‭are‬‭the‬‭occurrence‬‭of‬‭positive‬‭peptides‬‭in‬‭each‬
‭group.‬

‭AUC.‬ ‭Two‬ ‭dropout‬ ‭rates‬ ‭were‬ ‭tested;‬ ‭0‬ ‭(no‬ ‭dropout)‬ ‭and‬ ‭0.6.‬ ‭Boxplots‬ ‭summarize‬ ‭the‬ ‭distribution‬ ‭of‬ ‭the‬
‭performance‬‭of‬‭20‬‭cross-validation‬‭models.‬‭Whiskers‬‭extend‬‭to‬‭the‬‭largest/smallest‬‭performance‬‭no‬‭further‬‭than‬‭a‬
‭distance‬ ‭of‬
‭from‬ ‭the‬ ‭hinge.‬ ‭Potential‬ ‭outliers‬ ‭are‬ ‭defined‬ ‭as‬ ‭values‬ ‭with‬ ‭a‬ ‭distance‬ ‭greater‬ ‭than‬
‭1‬. ‭5‬ · ‭𝐼𝑄𝑅‬
‭from‬‭the‬‭hinge‬‭and‬‭are‬‭shown‬‭as‬‭circles.‬‭The‬‭averages‬‭taken‬‭over‬‭the‬‭20‬‭cross-validation‬‭models‬‭are‬
‭1‬. ‭5‬ · ‭𝐼𝑄𝑅‬
‭shown as crosses.‬

‭PPV.‬ ‭Two‬ ‭dropout‬ ‭rates‬ ‭were‬ ‭tested;‬ ‭0‬ ‭(no‬ ‭dropout)‬ ‭and‬ ‭0.6.‬ ‭Boxplots‬ ‭summarize‬ ‭the‬ ‭distribution‬ ‭of‬ ‭the‬

==PAGE:84==
‭Fig.‬ ‭B.21.‬ ‭Difference‬ ‭in‬ ‭test‬ ‭performance‬ ‭between‬ ‭ESM-1b‬ ‭embedded‬ ‭FNN‬ ‭model‬ ‭and‬ ‭CNN‬ ‭model‬
‭measured‬‭by‬‭ΔAUC.‬‭The‬‭FNN‬‭model‬‭is‬‭the‬‭one‬‭with‬‭dropout.‬‭The‬‭performance‬‭of‬‭the‬‭CNN‬‭model‬‭is‬‭used‬‭as‬‭the‬
‭origin‬‭and‬‭the‬‭performance‬‭of‬‭the‬‭FNN‬‭model‬‭is‬‭given‬‭as‬‭ΔAUC‬‭relative‬‭to‬‭this‬‭origin.‬‭The‬‭per‬‭peptide‬‭difference‬
‭in‬ ‭performance‬ ‭is‬ ‭shown‬ ‭to‬ ‭the‬ ‭right,‬ ‭where‬ ‭peptides‬ ‭are‬ ‭sorted‬ ‭from‬ ‭the‬ ‭most‬ ‭abundant‬ ‭peptide‬ ‭to‬‭the‬‭least‬
‭abundant‬‭peptide‬‭only‬‭counting‬‭positive‬‭peptides.‬‭The‬‭difference‬‭in‬‭mean‬‭and‬‭weighted‬‭mean‬‭performance‬‭taken‬
‭over‬ ‭all‬ ‭peptides‬ ‭is‬ ‭shown‬ ‭to‬ ‭the‬ ‭left,‬ ‭where‬ ‭the‬ ‭weighted‬ ‭mean‬ ‭performance‬ ‭weights‬ ‭peptides‬ ‭after‬ ‭their‬
‭occurrence.‬‭Numbers‬‭in‬‭parentheses‬‭in‬‭labels‬‭along‬‭the‬‭first‬‭axis‬‭are‬‭the‬‭occurrence‬‭of‬‭positive‬‭peptides‬‭in‬‭each‬
‭group.‬

‭Whiskers‬ ‭extend‬ ‭to‬ ‭the‬ ‭largest/smallest‬ ‭performance‬ ‭no‬ ‭further‬ ‭than‬ ‭a‬ ‭distance‬ ‭of‬
‭from‬ ‭the‬ ‭hinge.‬
‭1‬. ‭5‬ · ‭𝐼𝑄𝑅‬
‭Outliers‬ ‭are‬ ‭defined‬ ‭as‬‭values‬‭with‬‭a‬‭distance‬‭greater‬‭than‬
‭from‬‭the‬‭hinge‬‭and‬‭are‬‭shown‬‭as‬‭circles.‬
‭1‬. ‭5‬ · ‭𝐼𝑄𝑅‬
‭The averages taken over the 20 cross-validation models are shown as crosses.‬
‭89‬
==PAGE:94==
‭Fig.‬‭B.31.‬‭Difference‬‭in‬‭test‬‭performance‬‭between‬‭final‬‭version‬‭of‬‭models‬‭with‬‭new‬‭embeddings‬‭and‬‭the‬
‭baseline‬‭model‬‭measured‬‭by‬‭ΔAUC.‬‭In‬‭the‬‭final‬‭version‬‭of‬‭models‬‭with‬‭new‬‭embeddings‬‭an‬‭architecture‬‭size‬‭of‬
‭2X‬‭is‬‭used‬‭with‬‭a‬‭scaling‬‭factor‬‭of‬‭1/5,‬‭a‬‭learning‬‭rate‬‭of‬‭0.0005‬‭and‬‭the‬‭sigmoid‬‭activation‬‭function‬‭applied‬‭to‬‭the‬
‭convolutional‬ ‭layer‬ ‭for‬ ‭CDRs.‬ ‭The‬ ‭embeddings‬ ‭of‬ ‭the‬ ‭final‬ ‭models‬ ‭are‬ ‭ESM-1b,‬ ‭ProtT5-XL-U50‬ ‭and‬ ‭ESM-2‬
‭indicated‬‭by‬‭different‬‭colors.‬‭The‬‭performance‬‭of‬‭the‬‭baseline‬‭BLOSUM50-embedded‬‭model‬‭is‬‭used‬‭as‬‭the‬‭origin‬
‭and‬ ‭the‬ ‭performance‬ ‭of‬ ‭the‬ ‭other‬ ‭three‬ ‭models‬ ‭are‬ ‭given‬ ‭as‬ ‭ΔAUC‬ ‭relative‬ ‭to‬ ‭this‬ ‭origin.‬ ‭The‬ ‭per‬ ‭peptide‬
‭difference‬‭in‬‭performance‬‭is‬‭shown‬‭to‬‭the‬‭right,‬‭where‬‭peptides‬‭are‬‭sorted‬‭from‬‭the‬‭most‬‭abundant‬‭peptide‬‭to‬‭the‬
‭least‬‭abundant‬‭peptide‬‭only‬‭counting‬‭positive‬‭peptides.‬‭The‬‭difference‬‭in‬‭mean‬‭and‬‭weighted‬‭mean‬‭performance‬
‭taken‬ ‭over‬ ‭all‬ ‭peptides‬‭is‬‭shown‬‭to‬‭the‬‭left,‬‭where‬‭the‬‭weighted‬‭mean‬‭performance‬‭weights‬‭peptides‬‭after‬‭their‬
‭occurrence.‬‭Numbers‬‭in‬‭parentheses‬‭in‬‭labels‬‭along‬‭the‬‭first‬‭axis‬‭are‬‭the‬‭occurrence‬‭of‬‭positive‬‭peptides‬‭in‬‭each‬
‭group.‬
‭90‬
==PAGE:95==
